Current Commentary

A Turning Point in the Turmoil of Guangdong and Guangxi 17

— Gao

Since the news of the Guangdong and Guangxi troops halting their advance has spread, the unsettling situation on the Hunan border has calmed down, and the anxious atmosphere has eased. In addition to our burning anxiety, we also feel that the hope of reconciliation has not been extinguished, and it is not difficult to return to unity, stopping the fighting that has already begun and transforming hostility into peace. This can be said to be a blessing for the future of the nation and the country.

The disturbances in Guangdong and Guangxi began less than half a month ago. Although their public slogans were intended to avoid civil war, given the importance of the matter, it was easy to involve misunderstandings. The slightest error can be amplified a thousand miles. Not to mention the many voices that are like melting gold, only to fuel conjecture, even if everything is clarified, it is difficult to expect everyone to understand it thoroughly. Once the two sides lose their temper and go to extremes, it will become internal strife. Those who treat others as a snipe and a clam and regard themselves as a fisherman have already been laughing secretly from the sidelines. The original intention was to save the country, but the result was counterproductive. How could those involved have anticipated this? Fortunately, both sides are able to be aware of the current national crisis and strive to eliminate discord. The central government has spared no effort to offer repeated advice, and all parties have been exchanging letters in order to maintain peace. In the end, this has been able to turn the views of the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities and lead to the withdrawal of troops from Hunan. In today's dangerous situation, only unity can resist foreign aggression. How can internal strife be allowed to hasten destruction? The entire country has probably deeply understood this meaning, so it has been able to pull each other together and save the overall situation from danger. Perhaps there will be a further understanding of the meaning of unity from now on.

Furthermore, some say that although the cessation of the advance of the Guangdong and Guangxi armies has been confirmed, the process is still not clear enough to convince the public. Some speculate that they are changing course to other locations or that they have other plans. Such rumors can be ignored. We only hope that the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities, based on the meaning of unity, will make more concrete expressions: one side should withdraw troops to their original defenses in the shortest possible time, and the other side should select responsible representatives to attend the Second Plenary Session of the Central Committee, express their loyalty in planning for the country, and jointly plan for the great cause of national salvation. They should not repeat the trick of "朝四暮三 (giving someone four in the morning and three in the evening)," causing us further disappointment. The central government should also sincerely consider the difficulties of the times, adopt public opinion, and use a unified pace to respond consistently. If they stop at the brink of the precipice and mend the fold after the sheep is lost, then wouldn't this small setback be equivalent to firmly establishing the cornerstone of sincere unity?

Master of Classical Learning, Zhang Taiyan, Passes Away in Suzhou 18

Suffering from Gallbladder Inflammation, Passing at Sixty-Nine Years Old. Central Government Decides to Issue 3,000 Yuan for Funeral Expenses.

(Suzhou) Master of Classical Learning Zhang Taiyan passed away here this morning at 8:00 AM due to gallbladder inflammation, at the age of sixty-nine. Everyone far and near mourns. (14th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) National Studies Master Zhang Taiyan recently fell ill in Suzhou. Repeated consultations with renowned physicians failed to bring about a cure. By the morning of the 13th, his condition took a turn for the worse. His family immediately telegraphed relatives and friends in Beijing and Shanghai. After hearing the news, Liao Weifen traveled by train to visit him on the evening of the 13th. Unfortunately, Zhang passed away suddenly at 8:00 AM on the morning of the 14th. All circles in Beijing have expressed great sorrow upon receiving this news. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Suzhou) National Studies Master Zhang Taiyan had long suffered from gallbladder inflammation. Recently, upon hearing news from Guangdong and Guangxi, he was worried about national affairs, triggering his old illness. After seeking medical treatment, it was diagnosed as abdominal infection caused by nasal bacteria. His condition worsened on the evening of the 13th, and he passed away at 8:00 AM on the morning of the 14th. He left no last words. Zhang's relatives and friends have now formed a funeral affairs office and have scheduled the encoffining ceremony for 10:00 AM on the morning of the 16th. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tokyo) Ding Weifen went to Suzhou on the night of the 13th to visit Zhang Taiyan. After receiving news of Zhang's death in Beijing on the morning of the 14th, there was great mourning. The central government immediately decided to issue 3,000 yuan for funeral expenses and asked Ding to convey their condolences. The secretariat has telegraphed Ding, asking him to convey condolences to Madam Zhang nearby and to hand over the funeral expenses. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) After the news of Zhang Taiyan's death reached Beijing, the central government was deeply saddened. It was decided to issue 3,000 yuan for funeral expenses, and the Central Secretariat telegraphed Ding Weifen to convey condolences to Zhang's family. The original telegram is as follows: "To Ding Weifen, Committee Member, at Zhang's Residence in Suzhou: We were shocked to learn of Mr. Taiyan's sudden death this morning, and we are deeply saddened. The central government has decided to issue 3,000 yuan for funeral expenses and requests that you convey our condolences. The funds will be remitted separately. We hope that you will convey condolences to Madam Zhang nearby and hand over the funds upon arrival. (Signed) Secretariat of the Central Executive Committee." (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Suzhou) Telegram to the Shanghai Press Association and forwarded to all newspapers and organizations nationwide: Mr. Zhang Taiyan passed away at his residence in Suzhou at 8:00 AM on June 14. We respectfully report this news. Zhang's Funeral Affairs Office.

(Suzhou) Zhang Taiyan passed away at his residence in Suzhou at 8:00 AM on the 14th. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

A Brief Biography of Zhang 19

(Nanjing) A brief biography of National Studies Master Zhang Taiyan is as follows: Zhang Taiyan, named Binglin, originally named Jiang, was a native of Yuhang County, Zhejiang Province. He was born in the seventh year of the Tongzhi reign of the late Qing Dynasty (1868). In the late Qing Dynasty, he studied under Yu Yue and also inquired about learning from Huang Yizhou, adhering to oral learning. Because he read the "Donghua Records" and unofficial histories of the late Ming Dynasty, he embraced racial ideas. He studied the "Zuo Zhuan" and was recognized by Governor Zhang Zhidong of Hubei, who recruited him into his staff in the spring of the Wuxu year. He enjoyed talking about revolution and clashed with Liang Dingfen, so he returned to Shanghai to write for the "Changyan Bao." When the Wuxu Reform Movement arose, he sought refuge in Taiwan because he had written for the "Shiwu Bao," and wrote to caution Kang and Liang not to be loyal to foreign races. In the Jihai year, he traveled to Japan and met Mr. Sun Yat-sen, and they talked very compatibly. In the Gengzi year, he cut off his queue in Shanghai to show his determination. He then took refuge in Suzhou and lectured at Soochow University for nearly a year, which was discovered by Governor Enshou of Jiangsu. He fled to Japan again. In the Renyin year, he, Qin Lishan, Feng Ziyou, and others launched the 242nd Anniversary Memorial Meeting for the Fall of the Nation in Tokyo, and he personally wrote the declaration, which inspired many students studying abroad. In the Guimao year, he, Liu Shipei, Deng Shi, Huang Jie, and others founded the "National Essence Journal" in Shanghai, promoting national culture and advocating the restoration. When the Patriotic Study Society was established, he wrote for the "Subao," advocating revolution and expelling the Manchus. Because of his preface to Zou Rong's "Revolutionary Army," the Qing court launched a major purge, and he and Zou were imprisoned in the Western Prison. During his three years in prison, he delved into Buddhist scriptures and also wrote for the "China Daily" in Hong Kong. In the Bingwu year, he was released from prison and invited to Japan by the Tongmenghui, where he took charge of the "Min Bao." He often discussed matters with Hu Hanmin and Wang Jingwei at Mr. Sun Yat-sen's residence and gathered about twenty Chinese students in Tokyo to lecture on national studies. After the Wuchang Uprising in the Xinhai year, he returned to China. In the first year of the Republic of China, Mr. Sun Yat-sen welcomed him to Nanjing, where they met with great joy. He then went to Beijing, where Yuan Shikai hired him as a high-level advisor and subsequently appointed him as the special envoy for border affairs in the three northeastern provinces, but he did not take office. Three years later, he married Ms. Tang Guoli in Shanghai. After the Second Revolution, he returned to Beijing. At that time, Yuan stole the country, and because Mr. Zhang did not work for him, he imprisoned him. Five years later, after Yuan's death, Li Yuanhong released him and presented him with the four characters "束南樸學 (Puxue of Eastern Southern)." In the fourteenth year, he founded the "Huaguo Magazine." In the same year, he traveled to Hubei and Hunan to lecture and then returned to Shanghai. In the twenty-first year, at the invitation of his students, he traveled to Peiping. He returned south that summer and moved to Suzhou in the autumn. Colleagues loved to gather the National Studies Society and invite Mr. Zhang to lecture. In the twenty-fourth year, due to differing teaching philosophies, he established the Zhang's National Studies Lecture Hall and gave lectures year-round, and also founded the "Zhiyan" bi-monthly, which was supported by the central government with 10,000 yuan. Zhang was extremely knowledgeable in all books and was a master of writing. He did not favor Song poetry when discussing current affairs, and his study of phonology and etymology was extremely refined, revealing the essence of language and writing. His original work, "Zhang's Collected Works," was published. In the twenty-second year, his students published a sequel in Peiping. He lectured for nearly forty years, and his students were all over the country, the most famous being Huang Kan, Wu Chengshi, Zai Dong, Zhu Xifu, and Qian Xia. Kan died of illness last autumn. Mr. Zhang is currently sixty-nine years old. His wife is Ms. Tang Guoli, and he has two sons and three daughters. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Zai Dong, the Dean of the College of Arts at Central University and a highly accomplished student of Zhang Taiyan, was deeply saddened by the telegram about Zhang's death. On the evening of the 14th, he went to Suzhou to convey condolences to Zhang's family and discuss funeral arrangements. When the reporter visited Mr. Wang, Wang said that Mr. Taiyan's death was the greatest misfortune for the academic community in our country and an irreparable loss. Last year, Mr. Ji Gang passed away, and now Mr. Taiyan has passed away as well. My mood is very confused, and I cannot express even one ten-thousandth of his life's deeds. However, Mr. Taiyan's national studies, writings, and meritorious revolutionary deeds have long been well-known domestically and do not require me to say more. Wang also said that last year, Mr. Zhang was invited by the academic community in Beijing to lecture, but it was interrupted due to a nosebleed. The central government sent Ding Weifen to express condolences and sent 10,000 yuan for medical treatment. Mr. Zhang used this money for lectures in Suzhou. Although he gradually recovered, his health continued to weaken. He had a long-standing asthma condition, which worsened. Due to the severity of his condition, his family telegraphed Mr. Zhang Puquan in Beijing on the 14th to describe his condition. Zhang was in Shaanxi, so Ding Weifen went to Suzhou to visit him. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 14th, he received a telegram from Ding stating that Mr. Zhang had passed away on the morning of the 14th. (14th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Treatment Process 20

Suzhou Correspondence: Mr. Zhang Taiyan, a master of erudition, currently residing at No. 50 Jinfan Road, Suzhou, passed away today (the 14th) at 8:00 AM due to nasal mycosis and cholecystitis, at the age of 69. A description of his illness and a brief history are as follows:

In the 23rd year of the Republic of China, Mr. Zhang moved from his residence on Tongfu Road, Shanghai, to a newly built house on Jinfan Road, Suzhou. He founded the Zhang Family National Studies Lecture Hall and published the "Zhiyan" bi-monthly, which became famous nationwide. Many people came to Suzhou to attend his lectures. Prominent figures in Suzhou, such as Li Yinquan, Zhang Zhongren, Chen Shiyi, and Jin Songcen, also strongly supported Mr. Zhang's National Studies Association. The central government provided Mr. Zhang with ten thousand yuan in funding last year. After establishing the National Studies Association, Mr. Zhang also advocated for national salvation through education, which was supported by those advocating for the revival of ancient traditions. This spring, Chen Jitang of Guangdong also sent representatives to Suzhou to invite Mr. Zhang to teach at the Xuehai Shushe in Guangdong. Mr. Zhang declined due to his advanced age and inability to travel. At the same time, the central government also considered inviting Mr. Zhang to preside over the National History Museum, which he also declined. Due to his advanced age, Mr. Zhang would only accept invitations from schools and organizations in Suzhou to give lectures occasionally. He could not stand for long, so he had to sit while lecturing, which would often cause him to pant. Mr. Zhang had suffered from nasal mycosis for nearly twenty years, and numerous treatments had been ineffective. In the past four years, his asthma had worsened daily, leading to a decline in his physical strength. Two weeks ago, a fungus in his nostril suddenly fell off, and he immediately felt unwell and had a poor appetite. Starting on the 13th of this month, he began to experience chills and fever, with his temperature reaching a high of 105 degrees. Initially, he consulted Xie Jianxin, a chiropractor, for massage therapy. Subsequently, Yu Yunxiu, a doctor from Shanghai, came to Suzhou to diagnose and treat him, along with Western doctors Wang Jidao, Lin Sumin, and Sun Jianyi. They diagnosed his condition as cholecystitis, malaria, and complications from nasal mycosis and asthma. However, Mr. Zhang was inherently active, so that day he still went from his bedroom upstairs to the reception room downstairs to talk to people. Li Yinquan, a recluse from Xiaowang Mountain, and Ding Weifen, a committee member in Beijing, came to Suzhou to visit Mr. Zhang upon hearing the news. Unexpectedly, at 7:45 AM today (the 14th), Mr. Zhang passed away suddenly. When Mr. Zhang was on his deathbed, Ding Weifen, Li Yinquan, colleagues from the National Studies Association, his wife Madam Tang Guoli, and his children were all present. Because Mr. Zhang did not think he would die immediately, he did not prepare a formal will. However, Mr. Zhang had told his friends and disciples that he hoped that after his death, they would find a way to permanently maintain the Zhang Family National Studies Lecture Hall that he had established, so that the national studies he had devoted his life to could be passed on. Currently, his friends have established a funeral affairs office at Mr. Zhang's residence and are sending telegrams to relatives and friends at home and abroad to announce the death. The coffin will be sealed on the 16th. The funeral arrangements will depend on the agreement after his close friend Zhang Ji comes to Suzhou. Mr. Zhang's surviving family members include his wife Madam Tang Guoli, two sons, the eldest Zhang Dao, 20 years old, currently studying at Datong University in Shanghai, married to Peng, the second son Zhang Qi, 13 years old, and two daughters, the eldest Zhang Zhuo, deceased, the second Zhang , married to Zhu Jinzhou, currently the Director of the Finance Department of Gansu. Mr. Zhang devoted his life to the study of national studies, was proficient in phonology and etymology, loved the Spring and Autumn Annals (Zuo Zhuan), and strictly adhered to the teachings of his teachers. He had strong nationalistic sentiments and admired Liu Bowen's assistance to the Ming dynasty in overthrowing the Yuan dynasty and restoring the Han people. Therefore, he had said before his death that he wished to be buried next to Liu Bowen's tomb in Wenzhou. His works include "Qiuyan," "Zhang's Series," "Supplement to Zhang's Series," "Xuelin Yayan," and "Jianlun," among others. Zhang Binglin's original name was Yi, with the courtesy names Meishu and Taiyan. He was a native of Yuhang County, Zhejiang. In his youth, he studied under Yu Quyuan (Yue), a great Confucian scholar in Zhejiang. He once took the county examination but dropped out due to illness. He then abandoned his ambition for an official career and devoted himself to the study of national studies. At the age of twenty-seven, he joined the Qiangxuehui initiated by Kang Zuzhao and began to write articles for Shanghai newspapers, expressing his opinions. In the year of Bing Shen (1897), he and Liang Qichao were responsible for writing for the Shanghai Shibao. In the year of Wu Xu (1899), he entered the staff of Zhang Zhidong, the governor of Hubei, and then served as the editor-in-chief of the Changyan Bao. He was wanted by the Qing government due to political persecution and fled to Taiwan. In the year of Yi Hai, he met Sun Yat-sen and discussed revolution, opposing Kang Youwei and others' protection of the Qing dynasty. In the year of Geng Zi, he joined the Shanghai Guohui and was again wanted by the Qing government. He then sought refuge at Soochow University, established by Christians in Suzhou. Due to his radical essays, he was again resented by the authorities. In the year of Xin Chou, he polished translations at the Guangzhi Bookstore in Tokyo, Japan. In the year of Ren Yin, he and Feng Ziyou initiated a memorial meeting in Tokyo for the 242nd anniversary of the fall of China. In the year of Gui Mao (1903), he served as a writer for the Shanghai Guocui Xuebao, advocating nationalism. He and Zou Rong wrote "The Revolutionary Army," which again incurred the Qing government's resentment. He was arrested by the authorities of the foreign concession and imprisoned in the Western Prison for three years. After being released from prison in the year of Bing Wu, he served as the editor-in-chief of the Min Bao and traveled to the United States to promote the Xinhai Revolution. After returning to China from the United States, he was summoned to Beijing after the establishment of the Nanjing government in the first year of the Republic of China. Zhang was very dissatisfied when Sun Yat-sen ceded his position to Yuan Shikai. He then resided in Shanghai until he moved to Suzhou in the 23rd year of the Republic of China and formed the National Studies Lecture Hall. He passed away on June 14th of the 25th year of the Republic of China. (June 14th)

Doctor's Report 21

(Special Dispatch from this City) Regarding the news of Mr. Zhang Taiyan's death, according to Dr. Yu Yunxiu's report, on the 12th (Friday) morning, he received a phone call from Suzhou saying that Mr. Zhang was ill. He went to Suzhou in the afternoon, around 3:00 PM, he had a slight fever (37.1 degrees Celsius) and chills, felt nauseous, and had some tenderness and resistance in the upper right abdomen. His tongue was brown and extremely dry. He had had a poor appetite for more than a month, and there was a suspicion of stomach cancer. However, because he had had a gallstone attack several years ago, it was also possible that the gallstones had recurred. At that time, he prescribed antipyretic, pain-relieving, appetite-stimulating, and heart-strengthening medications. When he was about to return to Shanghai (6:00 PM), he re-examined him and found that his fever had risen and he was vomiting, but only a small amount of mucus was vomited. He originally planned to go again on Sunday, but on Saturday he received another phone call saying that he had a high fever and chills, so he was asked to go for a consultation immediately. Due to his busy schedule with patients in Shanghai, he could not leave in the afternoon. In the evening at 8:00 PM, Mr. Zhang's third daughter (Mrs. Zhu Duomin) returned from Suzhou and said that the fever had subsided, he was asking for food, and his mind was clear, but his pulse was faster. So he decided to go to Suzhou early Sunday morning, but he had already passed away. It was said that after the fever subsided, he had another bout of chills and high fever up to 41 degrees Celsius after only a few hours. Doctors from the North Pole Hospital injected heart-strengthening drugs all night to maintain him until about 7:30 AM on Sunday morning, when he passed away. Doctors in Suzhou suspected malaria (but no malaria parasites were found in the blood test, but only tested once) or a recurrence of gallstones. Due to the rapid and violent onset, his advanced age, and weak heart, he passed away suddenly. A definite diagnosis was difficult. Also, during the chills and fever on Saturday morning, at about 10:00 AM, he suddenly had difficulty breathing and almost passed out. He then vomited a piece of something that looked like meat but wasn't. His breathing immediately returned to normal. Doctors in Suzhou examined it and found that it was a nasal polyp that had fallen off and entered the throat from the nose. It was said that Mr. Zhang had suffered from nasal polyps for more than ten years and had had surgery twice. (June 14th)

Sangshima's Remarks 22

The Japanese Military and Foreign Ministry are United on China Policy: The Abolition of Eastern Hebei Requires Considerable Study

(Beiping) Sangshima, the Director of the East Asia Bureau of the Japanese Foreign Ministry, will visit Song Zheyuan at the Foreign Affairs Building tomorrow morning to exchange general Sino-Japanese opinions. On the morning of the 16th, he will accompany Shimizu, the counselor of the Japanese Embassy, to Zhangcheng by Japanese military plane for inspection and will return to Beiping that night. Song hosted a banquet for Sangshima and Sugiyama Gen, the Vice Chief of Staff of the Japanese Army, as well as Nagami, the Chief of Staff of the Japanese Garrison in Tianjin, and Matsumuro at the Summer Palace this afternoon, inviting Qin Decun, Chen Juesheng, Shimizu, Okuda, Hamada, and others to accompany them. Sangshima said that he had been away from China for three years and that the situation in China had changed a lot. The purpose of his visit to China was to inspect the latest situation in China and provide reference for future work. His planned itinerary includes Jijing, Pinglu, Jiqing, and various places in Shanghai and Beijing, and then he will return home from Shanghai. He had already met with Tashiro and the chiefs of staff in Tianjin and listened to their statements on the current situation in Jizhou. The local Chinese authorities in North China should seek the happiness and stability of the people in their current political affairs, and the Japanese authorities should also assist in their efforts. Most of the cotton used by Japanese spinning mills is purchased from the United Kingdom, the United States, and Egypt. If Chinese cotton is improved and sold to Japan, it will not only improve the lives of the Chinese people, but also promote the economic cooperation between Japan and China. The relationship between China and Japan must be adjusted. According to his observation, the goal of comprehensive adjustment can be achieved in the future. Regarding the issue of personnel in various departments in North China being responsible for negotiations, the Japanese military and the Foreign Ministry have a consistent policy toward China and there is no distinction. The situation in North China is special. Whether the military or the Foreign Ministry is responsible for negotiations, they act in unison. In his opinion, the Eastern Hebei issue should be merged with the Hebei-Chahar government immediately. In principle, it cannot exist permanently, but the timing of the merger of the two governments requires considerable study before it can be realized. Although the increase in the number of Japanese troops stationed in North China has caused panic among the people in various parts of China, it is actually for the purpose of protecting overseas Chinese. He asserted that the Japanese side has no intention of armed aggression. (Special Dispatch on the 14th)

(Beiping) When Sangshima, the Director of the East Asia Bureau of the Japanese Foreign Ministry, met with reporters from Chinese newspapers today, someone asked whether Tokyo's policy on North China was handled by the Foreign Ministry or the Army Ministry. Sangshima admitted that various issues in North China were handled by the Army Ministry, but said that the Foreign Ministry and the Army Ministry definitely held the same policy. (Reuters Dispatch on the 14th)

Meierhe Submits a Reply to the Ministry of Finance on the Penalty Method for Transporting Gold 29

(Nanjing) Inspector General of Customs Meierhe replied to the Ministry of Finance that, after investigation, gold bullion is valuable and small in size. If merchants hide gold bars tightly on their bodies, it is not easy for customs officers to detect them. Therefore, those who transport gold into and out of various ports often hide them on their bodies in an attempt to avoid customs declaration and the procedures for requesting a guarantee from the chamber of commerce. The government strictly handles the transportation of gold bullion by merchants. If anyone fails to comply with the regulations, the customs can confiscate the gold bullion they transport and turn it over to the public. Now, in order to be considerate of the difficulties of merchants, and for those who have no definite evidence of attempting to smuggle gold overseas, it is proposed to handle the matter leniently and impose a fine of 30% of the value of the gold bullion they transport and exempt them from confiscation. (Special Dispatch on the 14th)

Antiquities Preservation Committee Passes More Than 30 Draft Resolutions 30

(Nanjing) The Central Antiquities Preservation Committee held its 14th meeting on the 13th, attended by Zhang Daofan, Li Ji, Ma Heng, Jiang Fukui, Huang Wenqiang, Teng Gu, Zhu Xizu, Qiu Shanyuan, He Tianjian, Su Chushi, Yuan Tongli, Chen Nianzhong, etc. The proposals were reviewed in four groups: 1. Regulations, 2. Preservation, 3. Investigation and Rewards, 4. Government Plans. The afternoon continued and passed more than 30 draft resolutions, the important ones being that important private antiquities scattered abroad should be nationalized as soon as possible, and rules should be formulated for the management of the export of private antiquities and the establishment of branch associations in various places. (Special Dispatch on the 14th)

Statistics on the Price of Farmland Throughout the Country 33

(Nanjing) The Agricultural Experiment Institute has received reports on land prices from 882 counties in 22 provinces, including Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Qinghai, Shaanxi, Gansu, Shanxi, Hebei, Shandong, Jiangsu, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Sichuan, Yunnan, Guizhou, Hunan, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, Fujian, Guangdong, and Guangxi. The highest price per mu of paddy field is 200 yuan, the average is 43 yuan, and the lowest is 1 yuan. The highest price per mu of dry land in the plains is 200 yuan, the average is 25 yuan, and the lowest is 1 yuan. The highest price per mu of dry land in the mountains is 100 yuan, the average is 13 yuan, and the lowest is 1 yuan. From the 20th to the 24th year, the price of paddy fields fell by 17%, and the price of mountain land fell by 18%. (Special Dispatch on the 14th)

Canceling Sanctions Against Italy: "He Who Tied the Bell Must Untie It." European Countries Request the UK to Take the Lead. The UK's Attitude Awaits Formal Decision. 35

(London) A general movement to cancel sanctions against Italy is underway in Europe. It is reported that European capitals have telegraphed London, requesting the British government to take the lead in proposing this. At the same time, diplomatic representatives of European countries have also notified the British government that member states of the League of Nations consider sanctions to have failed and are only waiting for the UK to initiate their cancellation, since their implementation was originally proposed by the UK. Czech President Benes stated that the Czech Republic remains a firm supporter of collective action but feels that it is now imperative to cancel sanctions and allow Italy to return to the League of Nations. However, the Czech Republic is unwilling to take the lead in proposing this, as it believes that this is the responsibility of the UK and France. It is reported that the attitude of Soviet Russia is even more definite. Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov stated that the danger in Europe today stems solely from Germany's militarism. Italy is now willing to join the common front of resistance, and the threat of sanctions must be terminated. Litvinov also requested the UK to set an example, as the implementation of sanctions was mainly promoted by British Foreign Secretary Eden. At the same time, British Foreign Office staff are currently busy drafting a plan to reform the League of Nations. It is reported that this plan is based on the establishment of regional agreements, so that Geneva is no longer responsible for handling regional disputes. It is widely believed that the UK may submit this proposal at the next League of Nations General Assembly meeting. It is reported that at the meeting of the House of Commons next Monday, some members will ask Foreign Secretary Eden about the Prime Minister's recent remarks in the House of Commons regarding sanctions against Italy. Political circles now feel that diplomatic affairs should be debated as soon as possible, and journalists close to political circles now believe that this debate will be held on June 22, and there is information that it may be held even earlier. (Reuters Dispatch on the 14th)

Before the Mediterranean Problem is Resolved, Loans to Italy from the UK are Unlikely to Materialize 36

(London) Financial figures expect that the current sanctions against Italy will be quickly lifted. However, Italy's move to borrow money from the UK will not materialize until the Mediterranean problem is definitively resolved. Political figures also said that the cabinet should make a definite decision on the following three issues soon: 1. Abolishing sanctions, 2. Not recognizing Italy's annexation of Abyssinia, 3. Revising the League of Nations Covenant. As for the reports in some newspapers tonight that there is a significant disagreement within the cabinet regarding the sanctions issue, and that a small number of cabinet members oppose Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain's proposal to cancel sanctions, well-informed sources indicate that this may not be true. (Havas Dispatch on the 13th)

The Argentine Government Will Issue a Declaration Explaining its Position on the League of Nations 37

Buenos Aires, Argentina: Rumors that the Argentine government's recent request for an early convocation of the League of Nations General Assembly was at the behest of a certain major power have been scoffed at by officials, who said that the government's actions are fully in line with the principles it has traditionally adhered to. According to this agency's reporters, the Argentine government will issue a declaration explaining the country's position at Geneva. The main points are that Argentina does not feel interested in the colonial issue and does not wish to interfere with the solution of the Italy-Abyssinia problem. Its only goal is to cooperate in maintaining world peace and maintaining its long-standing friendship with both the UK and Italy. As for whether Argentina is willing to recognize the established fact of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia after the League of Nations General Assembly is convened, and whether Argentina proposes to maintain or strengthen the current sanctions, there is currently no definite news. (Havas Dispatch on the 13th)

British Air Secretary Endorses Collective Security and Strengthens National Defense to Suit the UK's Needs 38

(London) Air Secretary Lord Swinton delivered a speech at Lock Park near Bobby City yesterday, discussing the international situation. He said, "If war breaks out, no matter who wins, both sides will ultimately lose. It is not possible for other countries to adopt a policy of isolation." The obligations undertaken by the signatory countries of the League of Nations Covenant must be fully fulfilled. Some say that the League of Nations has failed, but this is not the case. If the League of Nations can be based on realistic circumstances, it will not fail. Otherwise, failure is inevitable. If the general non-realists force the League of Nations to do what it cannot do or what it does not want to do, then the League of Nations will undoubtedly fail. Lord Swinton then mentioned the issue of regional mutual assistance agreements, saying that this agreement would not only not be weakened but could gradually be strengthened. "In short, the actions we should take diplomatically and defensively are to make the League of Nations an institution that is consistent with reality, and our national defense can also meet our needs." Little Entente Chiefs of Staff Conference 41

The First Annual Meeting was Held in Romania's Capital Yesterday to Discuss Jointly Establishing Factories to Manufacture Machinery

Bucharest, Romania: When the heads of state of the Little Entente countries, namely King Carol of Romania, President Benes of the Czech Republic, and Prince Paul, the first regent of Yugoslavia, held a meeting on the 7th of this month, they decided that the chiefs of staff of the armies of each country should hold a meeting for one day each year. The Question of Restoring Armaments in the Dardanelles Strait 42

The Lausanne Treaty Signatories Will Meet to Discuss It, and Turkey is Preparing to Propose a New Draft Agreement

Ankara, Turkey: The signatory countries of the Lausanne Treaty are scheduled to hold a meeting in Montreux, Switzerland, on the 22nd of this month to discuss the issue of re-fortifying the Dardanelles and Bosphorus straits. Semi-official figures here believe that the Turkish government will submit a new draft agreement at that time to replace the Lausanne Treaty. The content will be divided into three items: (A) Regarding Turkey's general security, namely, the abolition of the clauses of the Lausanne Treaty regarding the abolition of armaments in the two straits; merchant ships are free to pass through the straits; civilian and military aircraft are prohibited from flying over the straits; (B) Regarding the security of the two straits, namely, the tonnage of foreign warships wishing to pass through the straits shall be limited to 14,000 tons; submarines are prohibited from passing; (C) Regarding the security of the Black Sea, namely, warships belonging to non-coastal countries passing through the straits shall be limited to invitations; their total tonnage shall not exceed 28,000 tons. In addition, it is stipulated that foreign warships wishing to pass through the straits must notify the Turkish government one month in advance. (Havas Dispatch on the 14th)

People's Front Parades to Celebrate Victory, The Internationale and the Marseillaise Resound Together

(Paris) After the resolution of the strike in French major industries, the people's hearts were greatly comforted at the end of the week. A small portion of the labor unrest remains to be resolved. Judging from the current situation, Prime Minister Blanc expects everything to return to normal by the beginning of next week. However, the owners of major stores in Amiens, Toulouse, and Toren would rather close their doors and let employees take holidays than have shop assistants stay in the store without working. Labor unrest has even spread to Morocco. (Fourteenth Reuters News Agency)

(Paris) Since the metallurgical workers reached an agreement with the capitalists and left the factories, the strike situation has clearly eased. Barbers reached an agreement with their employers this morning and will resume work tomorrow. Strikers in the capital and provinces who obtained satisfactory resolutions last night and left the factories marched in teams this morning to celebrate "the great victory of the People's Front." There were 20,000 participants in Le Havre, 100,000 in Bordeaux, and 6,000 in Cherbourg, all led by the Communist red flag and the French tricolor flag, with marching bands playing the Marseillaise (French national anthem) and the Internationale (Communist Party anthem) in a lively atmosphere. However, there were no disturbances anywhere. The organizers had installed loudspeakers in advance on the main thoroughfares, telling the workers as they passed by, "When you are struggling, you can strictly observe order and discipline, and maintain dignity. Now that you have won, you should still maintain this spirit." At present, only major clothing stores, food stores, and insurance companies are still on strike. In addition, dockworkers, porters, and stevedores in various ports suddenly announced a strike yesterday, demanding improved treatment, so activities in various ports have come to a standstill. (Fourteenth Havas Telegraph)

(Paris) This afternoon, the People's Front held demonstrations in various places to celebrate "the victory of the striking workers." The situation was very stable. There were 10,000 demonstrators in Nîmes, 5,000 in Belfort, 1,000 in Lorient, and thousands in Toulon, all marching in teams through the streets, singing loudly, and local members of parliament or pro-labor mayors giving speeches, before dispersing without disturbances. Finally, the announcement also stated that certain groups, especially right-wing veterans' organizations, namely the Croix-de-Feu, are attempting to form independent trade unions. Feeling the Threat from the Soviet Union, Japan Plans to Actively Expand its Military 49

Minister of the Army Terauchi Plans to Advise Hirota; Soviet Forces Increased to 1.3 Million; Far Eastern Military Industry Self-Sufficient

(Tokyo) Recently, the Soviet Union has actively expanded its military in the Far East, which has drawn great attention from the Japanese Army. In order to consolidate national defense and cope with this move by the Soviet Union, there is a strong sense of the need to quickly strengthen military preparations, and at least to realize and strengthen comprehensive national defense capabilities in the shortest possible time in order to cope with the situation. At the time of the Manchurian Incident, the Soviet Union had only about 500,000 regular Red Army soldiers, but this year it has increased to 1.3 million, and it is devoting all its efforts to strengthening new weapons. This year's military budget has reached 14.8 billion rubles, and efforts are being made to expand the powerful air force and accelerate the tank forces, with approximately 5,000 aircraft and 4,000 tanks. The total force will reach 100 divisions, forming an unparalleled military force. After completing the double-track engineering of the Siberian Railway, the heavy industry and power generation areas in the Far East will also be completed, so that most of the weapons and military supplies in the Soviet Far East can be self-sufficient. The Soviet Union's expansion of its military and completion of military facilities is clearly aimed at Japan, and Japan's preparations in this regard are very weak. If this trend continues, the Soviet Union's military dominance in the Far East will greatly increase, which is inevitable. It may bring significant obstacles to Japan's future, which cannot be ruled out. Therefore, Japan should respond to the heavy pressure of Soviet military preparations with great determination and increase military preparations as soon as possible, which is unavoidable for national defense. The Army authorities will proceed with a firm determination based on the above conclusions in order to achieve the goal. Recently, Minister of the Army Terauchi will present this opinion to Prime Minister Hirota. (Fourteenth Allied Telegraph)

To Cope with the Pacific Situation, Taiwan Governor-General System to Change to Military Official System 50

Because the naval forces of the United Kingdom and the United States will inevitably pursue their active policies in the Pacific due to the natural expiration of the Pacific defense limitation clause, Japan must cope with this matter and ensure the security of the South. This is an urgent matter to overcome the extraordinary situation. Therefore, if the position and authority of the military Governor-General are not upgraded, such as the current Governor-General of Korea under the command of the Minister of Colonial Affairs, transforming into an independent personnel administration, then the true rule of Taiwan is impossible. Therefore, it is advocated to first amend the official systems of the Ministry of Colonial Affairs and the Taiwan Governor-General's Office. As for the successor of Governor-General Nakagawa, Admiral Nomura Kichisaburo and Admiral Kobayashi Seizo are the most likely. (Fourteenth Allied Telegraph)

Japanese Army Ministry Announces Border Conflict Incidents 51

Eighty-Two Incidents in Five Months; Plans to Demand Russia Withdraw Troops from the Far East

(Tokyo) The Army Ministry announced on the 13th the statistics and contents of the "Manchukuo"-Mongolia and "Manchukuo"-Soviet border incidents that occurred from January to mid-May of this year. According to the statistics, there were 35 incidents on the eastern border, 27 on the northern border, 4 on the western border, and 16 on the "Manchukuo"-Mongolia border, totaling 82 incidents, an increase of 47 incidents compared to 35 incidents in the same period last year. The military is very concerned about the sharp increase in border disputes and is considering appropriate countermeasures. The reason is that since the inspection by Gaganochitchi, the Soviet military in the Far East has rapidly strengthened its military preparations and completed its fortresses this year. It is well aware that it is in a far superior position to Japan, so it does not hesitate to try. Therefore, if the Soviet Union does not withdraw its military from the Far East, such incidents will continue to occur in the future. In view of this, the military feels that the Treaty of Non-Aggression proposed by the Soviet Union has no security guarantees whatsoever. The most effective solution to eliminate disputes is to invoke Article 9 of the Treaty of Portsmouth, requiring the Soviet Union to abolish artillery positions and set up an demilitarized zone within 50 miles of the border line. Otherwise, the only way is to make the power of the two countries on the border equal. There is no other way. (Fourteenth Allied Telegraph)
