Details are as follows:

Board of Directors and Supervisors Meeting: The association held a joint meeting of the Board of Directors and Supervisors at the association's office yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. More than ten directors and supervisors attended, including Shen Yong, Zou Shisong, Yuan Qixiang, Yuan Guisheng, Chen Baoxiang, Zhou Chuanzeng, Ke Hua, and General Director Ge Futian. The meeting was chaired by Shen Yong, with Xu Chengde as the recording secretary. After the formal opening ceremony, the following reports were presented: General Director Ge reported on negotiations with the Municipal Council regarding vehicle modifications; the secretariat reported on the letter to the Municipal Council and recent association affairs. Subsequently, the following cases were discussed: Regarding the tire modification issue, the Municipal Council has not yet responded to the association's request. How should this be addressed? Resolved: Send a letter to the Taxpayers’ Association and all Chinese directors and committee members, requesting them to negotiate with the Municipal Council. Inform members not to panic and to quietly await a resolution before the new regulations are implemented. The case of consolidating members' unpaid membership fees was discussed and resolved to issue separate notices for collection. The meeting adjourned.

Letter Requesting Negotiations: The association sent a letter to the Shanghai Ratepayers’ Association of the Public Concession yesterday, stating that the association is negotiating with the Public Concession Municipal Council regarding the modification of tires and the weight restrictions on three-wheelers, requesting consideration of the difficult times and flexible handling. It stated that the announcement by your Bureau regarding the modification of three-wheeler tires to be implemented on July 1st has caused significant impediments to the association's members in terms of use and economy, causing deep anxiety and numerous requests to your Bureau to suspend implementation. The reasons why members cannot accept the modifications are summarized as follows: The old-fashioned wheels of three-wheelers are lightweight and suitable, and there has never been any inappropriateness. If wider, three-and-a-half-inch angled iron wheels are added, they will inevitably be clumsy and heavy, making it difficult to operate. If rubber tires are installed, the unevenness of the roads will make them inconvenient to try and use. In addition, each set of rubber tires costs at least 16 national dollars and can only be used for one year, which is several times more expensive than the old-fashioned iron wheels, which cost only 3 national dollars per set and can be used for more than ten years. In terms of the cost of building a three-wheeler, it does not exceed 20 dollars. Now the price of one wheel is so high that, in the current situation of economic depression and declining business, how can those who earn a living by the sweat of their brow suddenly bear such a burden? Therefore, in fact, it is impossible to accept either the modification of iron wheels or rubber tires. As for the weight restriction on three-wheelers, due to the excessive restrictions, violations occur frequently, causing unspeakable pain in business. It should be requested that the load limit for single-person vehicles be set at 700 pounds, and the load limit for double-person vehicles be set at 1,000 pounds. We have already appealed to you, and now we must inform you again, urging your Bureau to consider the hardship of the workers and the suffering of their lives, to suspend implementation and to handle the weight issue with flexibility. We, the three-wheeler industry, are already struggling to maintain a living in these difficult times. If we make more changes and add to the burden, it will be tantamount to forcing us to close down and driving people into a desperate situation. We dare to express our urgent words, imploring your association (Chinese directors and committee members) to consider the hardship of the workers and the suffering of their lives, to quickly negotiate and argue the case based on reason, so as to secure our business. We look forward to your help.

Ministry of Industry Plans to Establish a Rayon Factory 104

Plans have been drawn up and can be started as soon as the funds are available. The Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association has been notified of the approval.

The Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association believes that the import of rayon and other woven goods is increasing year by year, which has a significant impact on the production and sales of domestic silk. The Executive Committee has resolved to submit proposals to the Ministries of Finance, Interior, and Industry, suggesting that the import of foreign rayon and other woven goods be restricted in stages each year, and that a rayon factory be established, and that the use of domestic goods be promoted, in order to recover rights and block leaks. In addition to the approvals already received from the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Finance, the association has now received a reply from the Ministry of Industry, Business Letter No. 44651, which states that a telegram from Qin on May 27, 1936, was received, requesting that the import of rayon and other woven goods be restricted and banned in stages each year, and that a rayon factory be established, and that the use of domestic goods be promoted. The contents of the Qin telegram have been noted. Regarding the promotion of the use of domestic goods, in addition to government officials, a committee for the use of domestic goods has already been established. The other points should be considered as the situation warrants and then dealt with if necessary. As for the request to establish a rayon factory, detailed plans have already been drawn up and can be started as soon as the funds are available. Also, the request to restrict and ban the import of foreign rayon and other woven goods cannot be implemented for the time being and should be considered later. You are hereby notified. Minister Wu Dingchang.

Two Homes Robbed in One Night in Hexi Township; Robbers Murder an Elderly Woman 110

Hexi Township, located south of Shanghai and belonging to Shanghai County, borders the Huangpu River to the south and Songjiang County to the west. On the night of the 12th of this month, a sudden robbery occurred, during which a 64-year-old woman was murdered. Due to the remote location, the incident was not reported to the county for investigation until yesterday, when news began to spread. The victims were identified as the Zhu Fusheng family, residing at No. 1, 7th Jia, 5th Bao, 1st District, and the Zhang Jinfa family, residing at No. 1, 6th Jia, 7th Bao. According to reports, there were six or seven robbers who first targeted the Zhu family at approximately 12 AM that night. However, because the Zhu family's house was newly built and the doors and windows were sturdy, they were unable to break in and fired several shots before abandoning the attempt. Subsequently, at around 2 AM, they broke into the Zhang Jinfa family's home, located about one mile from the previous location, and proceeded to rob them. The Zhang Jinfa couple happened to be out, leaving only a 64-year-old woman at home. The family was impoverished, with no valuables hidden away. When the robbers demanded money and were refused, they opened fire in frustration. The bullet entered through the lower abdomen and exited through the lower back. The elderly woman died yesterday morning from the gunshot wound. Township head Zhang Xinhe has collected the recovered bullet casings and reported the incident to the County Public Security Bureau for investigation. It is believed that the robbers came ashore from the Huangpu River and were unfamiliar with the area. The security team substation, originally established at Zhongdu Bridge, was removed last year, leaving the area vulnerable to theft and robbery.

Xingzhen ran home and told her husband, who tried to reason with him, advising her to be careful and avoid causing trouble. As a result, Xingzhen transferred to the Dechang Silk Factory. Rescheduled to the 22nd of This Month

Lawsuit Over the Rental Rights of the Mortgaged Film "Tears of a Cripple" 119

Hu Zhisheng, from Shanghai, organized the Yihua Song and Dance Troupe last year and toured the interior to perform. Unfortunately, business was poor, resulting in significant losses. He was forced to mortgage the film "Tears of a Cripple," consisting of ten reels and the license, to Yang Jinsheng, the owner of the Shengze Grand Theater (42 years old, from Songjiang, currently residing at No. 49 Zuojie, Songjiang County), for 128 yuan. It was agreed that the loan would accrue interest and the film would be screened by Yang. The proceeds would first be used to repay the principal of the loan, and any remaining funds would be returned to Hu Zhisheng. If the film was not screened, Hu could redeem it within three months. A contract was signed by both parties. Later, Yang exercised his rights and rented the film "Tears of a Cripple" to places like the Great World in Shanghai for screening. However, Hu Zhisheng claimed that Yang had not informed him beforehand and should not have rented the film for screening without permission. Therefore, he hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Special No. 2 Court, accusing Yang Jinsheng of fraud and breach of trust and requesting an investigation. After the court opened a trial and summoned the parties, it ruled that Yang Jinsheng was not guilty due to insufficient evidence presented by Hu. Hu was dissatisfied with the ruling and filed an appeal with the Third Branch of the High Court, but later withdrew the appeal. Yang Jinsheng believes that Hu Zhisheng should not have repeatedly made false accusations and that he has intentionally damaged his reputation. Therefore, he hired lawyer Sha Enpu to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Special No. 2 Court, accusing Hu Zhisheng of false accusation. The court accepted the complaint and Judge Zhang Chaozu presided over the trial in the Second Criminal Court the day before yesterday. The defendant was absent. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that the defendant often spread rumors, accusing the plaintiff of being untrustworthy and shameless for secretly screening his film. Therefore, he requested the arrest and prosecution of the defendant. After examining the statement, the court ordered the case to be temporarily suspended pending the plaintiff's confirmation of the defendant's address, after which another summons would be issued.

It is said that the YMCA believes that children are the masters of the future and that paying attention to children's health is fundamental to the revitalization of the nation. Therefore, they are holding this grand event to raise public awareness of children's health. All events are free of charge, and the public is welcome to participate. The schedule for the week is as follows: June 15th (Monday) 2 PM Opening Exhibition; 5 PM to 5:30 PM, Director of the Health Bureau, Mr. Li Ting'an, will give a speech; 5:30 PM, Huaien Primary School will perform; 6 PM, Municipal Council film; 16th (Tuesday) 9 AM to 4 PM Exhibition; 5 PM to 5:30 PM, Dr. Xu Nailing will give a lecture on "Children's Hygiene"; 5:30 PM, Qixiu Girls' School will perform English folk dance, Wan's Cartoons; 17th (Wednesday) 9 AM to 4 PM Exhibition; 5 PM to 5:30 PM, Dr. Gao Jingming will give a lecture on "Prevention and Treatment of Children's Gastrointestinal Diseases"; Municipal Council Primary School will perform a rhythmic band and a summer song for young soldiers, Municipal Council film, etc.; 18th (Thursday) 9 AM to 4 PM Exhibition; 5 PM to 5:30 PM, Tong Xingmen, from the Anti-Tuberculosis Association, will give a speech; 5:30 PM, Chongde Primary School will perform a piano solo, solo singing, a short drama, song and dance, and Wan's Cartoons; 19th (Friday) 9 AM to 4 PM Exhibition; 5 PM to 5:30 PM, Mr. Chen Tiesheng from the Ciyou Association will give a speech; 5:30 PM, Biwen Girls' School will perform and Municipal Council film; 20th (Saturday) 9 AM to 4 PM Exhibition and Games, Swimming, Jingzhi Troupe performances, etc.; 21st (Sunday) All-day Exhibition.

Court Prepares to Improve Delivery 122

Postal Service Sends Specialist to Court; Researching Procedures and Judicial Income

Jiang Yiping, a representative of the Shanghai Lawyers Association at the National Judicial Conference, proposed improving litigation delivery methods. It was decided that civil and criminal summonses, notifications, and judgments would be sent by the postal service instead of through bailiffs and judicial police, thereby completely eliminating delivery fees and travel expenses. However, transcription fees would still be collected. The method for collecting transcription fees would be for the parties to pay the fees first and then the judgments would be sent. All summons return receipts would be printed in a separate format, collected by the postman, and returned to the court. The Judicial Yuan would also consult with the Executive Yuan and instruct the Ministry of Transportation to order the postal service to send a postal worker to each court to manage the receipt and delivery of official documents and report return receipts. The duties of bailiffs and judicial police would be to apprehend criminals and seize property for search. This proposal has been set to take effect on July 1st. The Shanghai District Court has been preparing all procedures in recent days in order to implement it. However, this matter concerns the reform of national judicial procedures, and it is necessary to study the convenience and judicial revenue. Therefore, the Jiangsu High Court is discussing it.

News of Mr. Zhang Xiaolin's Sixtieth Birthday 123

*Shenshi News Agency Report* On the twenty-second of this month, it will be Mr. Zhang Xiaolin's sixtieth birthday. His relatives and friends, considering his blessings upon society and contributions to the Party and the nation, collectively planned a celebration. However, due to the unrest of the times and the economic depression, he repeatedly declined with humility, firmly refusing to accept. Later, through the gentle persuasion of Du Yuesheng, Yu Yefeng, Wang Xiaolai, Yang Hu, Qian Xinzhi, Liu Zhilu, and others, and at the suggestion of his son, Dr. Zhang Fayao, the gifts from all circles would be donated to the World Chinese Students' Association as a construction fund. Mr. Zhang then slightly revealed his willingness, but repeatedly urged that there should be no excessive extravagance. After this news spread, important figures from the Party and the nation, as well as prominent figures in society, joined the initiative one after another. The writer Zhang Shizhao was appointed to draft the birthday proclamation. The "Public Request for Articles Celebrating Mr. Zhang Xiaolin of Cixi's Sixtieth Birthday" recently published in various newspapers is his work. The initial list of initiators included Duan Zhiquan, Chiang Kai-shek, Xiao Focheng, Yu Youren, Du Yuesheng, Yu Yefeng, and one hundred others. Later, Wu Peifu, Jiang Zuobin, Chen Guofu, and three others joined, bringing the total to one hundred and three. On the first of this month, the Zhang Birthday Preparatory Office was formally established at 97 Avenue Edward VII (inside Linji Timber Company). Branch offices for receiving gifts were set up in Beijing, Tianjin, Nanjing, Hankou at the Bank of Communications, and in Zhang's residence at Yinmajing in Hangzhou. Du Yuesheng was appointed as the director of the preparatory committee, Wang Xiaolai as the deputy director, and Yu Yefeng as the general secretary, responsible for handling all necessary matters. It was divided into eight groups: Yu, the general secretary, concurrently served as the director of general affairs; Xu Caichen served as the director of accounting and general affairs; Qiu Fangmo served as the director of documentation; Mao Heyuan served as the director of decoration; Chu Minyi, Liu Zhilu, and Chen Qun served as the directors of reception; Jiang Gantang served as the director of security; Zhao Nansheng served as the director of banquets; and Wang Xiaolai concurrently served as the director of theatrical affairs. The presidium of the birthday hall has also been determined, including Yu Qiaqing, Huang Jinrong, Yang Xiaotian, Qian Xinzhi, Lin Kanghou, Yu Zuoting, Wang Xiaolai, Liu Weijun, Yu Yefeng, and Du Yuesheng, totaling ten people. It is also heard that the Peking opera circles of Beijing, Tianjin, and Shanghai, upon learning of Mr. Zhang's sixtieth birthday, all sent letters and telegrams requesting to participate in the celebratory performances. Those who have already joined include Mei Lanfang, Li Jihui, Ma Lianliang, Wang Youchen, Tan Xiaopei, Tan Fuying, Shang Xiaoyun, Xun Huisheng, Li Wanchun, Xin Yanqiu, and other famous performers. Many famous amateurs in the Shanghai opera circles are also participating. The birthday celebrations will be divided into three days: the 21st will be a warm-up for relatives and friends, the 22nd will be the actual birthday, and the 23rd will be for guests' entertainment. The birthday hall will be set up in the Great Shanghai Garden on Haige Road in West Shanghai, and decorations are currently being arranged. It is also heard that the organization of each group is very orderly, fearing that idlers may mix in. Therefore, guests who come to offer congratulations must wear badges so that the hosts can easily identify them.

Jiren Association to Found a Chinese Medicine Hospital 124

Since the Shanghai Jiren Aid Association (abbreviated as Jiren Association) began soliciting members, although it has been affected by the economic downturn, people from all walks of life, appreciating the new charter of the association, find that for each piece of wood contributed, members only need to bear five cents of the cost of making the wood, which is easy and affordable. Moreover, including the cost of lime, charcoal shavings, and carrying, it does not cost the bereaved family a penny and avoids any hint of charity. Therefore, those who agree to join the association are quite enthusiastic, and the Ren (Benevolence) Group is about to be established. Currently, members believe that when poor compatriots encounter illness, they lack the resources to consult doctors and take medicine, waiting helplessly for death. Their suffering is even greater than that of the deceased. Saving the dying and giving life should go hand in hand. They request the establishment of a free hospital to provide medical assistance and medicine to benefit the poor and sick. Therefore, the chairman, Shao Ruxin, has decided to cease the operation of the Dayun Hotel, which he founded, and transfer all three floors of the Western-style building, as well as the interior decoration, beds, bedding, etc., to the Jiren Association to establish the Jiren Chinese Medicine Hospital (located in Dakangfang on Baer Road in the French Concession, telephone 84533). Currently, they have secured the services of famous Shanghai doctors Xu Xiangchen, Cai Xunchen, Ren Nongxuan, Jiang Haifeng, and female doctor He Shiqing, among others, to voluntarily provide medical services in various departments. Once the Ren Group of the Jiren Aid Association is established, the Jiren Chinese Medicine Hospital can be realized.

Statistics of Cases Committed in This City Last Week 126

The Municipal Public Security Bureau announced that in the past week, a total of 317 criminal cases occurred within its jurisdiction, with a total of 554 male and female suspects arrested. The details are as follows: 19 robbery and extortion cases, involving 36 suspects; 87 theft cases, involving 133 suspects; 40 assault cases, involving 60 suspects; 10 rape and abduction cases, involving 20 suspects; 9 gambling cases, involving 20 suspects; 15 fraud cases, involving 27 suspects; 2 Communist Party cases, involving 3 suspects; 1 homicide case, involving 2 suspects; 2 arson cases, involving 3 suspects; 4 counterfeit currency cases, involving 4 suspects; 72 violation of police regulations cases, involving 126 suspects; and 60 other criminal cases, involving 106 suspects. In total, there were 317 cases involving 554 suspects. The above-mentioned suspects have all undergone preliminary trials by the Third Section. Except for 120 suspects in minor cases who were dealt with according to the Regulations on Punishment for Violations of Police Regulations or sentenced to release, the remaining suspects have been transferred to the local court or other competent authorities for trial. The number of criminal cases investigated this week has increased by 40 compared to last week, and the number of suspects arrested has increased by 130.

Record of the Re-election of the Petroleum Industry Association 128

The Shanghai Petroleum Industry Association, located at 7 Laobaidu Street, Wai Ma Road, Nanshi, held its third general membership re-election meeting yesterday at the Dahongyun Restaurant. Twenty-two member representatives, Huang Tiren from the Municipal Party Department, Zhang Dafu from the Social Affairs Bureau, Yuan Hongjun from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and more than forty guests attended. Ke Juchu was publicly elected as the chairman, and Chen Xi recorded the proceedings. After performing the customary rituals, the chairman delivered an opening speech and reported on the association's affairs and financial situation. Subsequently, representatives from higher authorities gave speeches. Then, the proposals were discussed:

* That a telegram be sent to the Central Government regarding the changes in the Southwest, seeking appropriate solutions through political means. Resolution: Passed.

* That a petition be submitted to the Ministry of Industry and the Legislative Yuan to promptly revise the association's organizational regulations to adapt to the needs of the environment. Resolution: Passed. Submitted to the General Assembly of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

* To request that all industries rectify their commercial ethics and eliminate false advertising. Resolution: Passed. Submitted to the General Assembly of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

At this point, the re-election was announced. As a result of the election, Jing Yimen, Chai Linsheng, Chen Yongnian, Xu Zhengde, Xie Boshu, Xu Jingqi, Zhu Jianqing, Han Ruiyu, and Fang Kunlin were elected as executive committee members; Qian Yinchao, Zhang Yuanheng, and Luo Jida were elected as alternate executive committee members; Huang Jiaosheng, Fan Shengquan, and Xu Qinbao were elected as supervisory committee members; and Ke Juchu was elected as an alternate supervisory committee member. After the election, they took an oath of office. By the time the dinner concluded and the meeting adjourned, it was already past nine o'clock.

Weather Report 134

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast for 4:30 PM yesterday stated: Hot weather with strong southeasterly and southwesterly winds, caused by a low-pressure system passing through Mongolia and moving eastward. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy and hot, with thunderstorms and variable winds. The low-pressure system in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River will move eastward. The East China Sea and Taiwan are cloudy, with local rain and strong southeasterly and southwesterly winds. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city reached a high of 92.1 degrees and a low of 70.9 degrees. On the same day last year, the high was 88.7 degrees and the low was 67.1 degrees.

Special Edition for the 15th Shanghai Municipal Health Movement

Today's Schedule 135

——Day 1——

10:00 AM: Opening Ceremony (at the People's Education Center), Opening of the Health Exhibition (at the People's Education Center)

11:00 AM: General Cleaning (Cleanliness Campaign Labor Service begins at the Chen Yingshi Memorial Pagoda in the West Gate District)

1:00 PM: Guidance on Children's Clothing Hygiene (at the People's Education Center), Cleanliness Campaign Labor Service in the West Gate District and the Hongkou District

4:00 PM to 4:30 PM: Commander Yang Xiaotian broadcasts a speech on the Central and Western Radio Station

4:50 PM to 5:10 PM: Director Li Ting'an broadcasts a speech on the Gospel Radio Station

5:30 PM to 6:00 PM: Mayor Wu broadcasts a speech on the Shanghai Municipal Government Radio Station

Declaration of the 15th Shanghai Municipal Health Movement Conference 136

This year is the Year of the Child. We hope everyone pays special attention to children's health! When it comes to children's health, we might as well first present the following figures:

(1) China has a population of 400 million, and 12 million people die each year (estimated at 30 per thousand of the total population), of which at least 4.8 million people (accounting for 40% of the deaths) are young children under the age of five.

(2) For every 1,000 births in China, 15 mothers die due to childbirth, and 200 infants under one year of age die.

(3) After physical examinations of children entering school in China, 85% are found to have deficiencies.

The reasons for the above staggering figures are related to economic conditions, but the lack of hygiene in daily life is the most pressing concern. Because in hygiene-conscious countries like Britain and the United States, the above figures have all been reduced by half compared to ours. Therefore, for this reason, we should: (1) Promote maternal and infant hygiene - implement prenatal and postnatal examinations, new-style delivery, infant clinics, home visits, Maternal and Infant Hygiene Association, Preschool Children's Hygiene Association, and other work - to reduce maternal and infant mortality rates and reduce the number of deaths of young children under the age of five. (2) Promote school hygiene - implement physical examinations, deficiency correction, vaccinations, disease treatment, and the development of hygienic habits - to prevent children's diseases and improve children's health.

Children are the masters of the future. When we promote hygiene, we should start with children's hygiene.

Health Campaign and Children's Health 137

— Wu Tiecheng

—A Message to the Citizens on the Occasion of the 15th Health Campaign Congress—

Fellow citizens! The annual health campaign is now being held again. However, given the current state of our nation and the increasingly tense international situation, we must not regard this health campaign as a mere annual formality. We should see this work as a means to revive the nation, save it from peril, and ensure its survival. Although the path may be difficult and filled with obstacles, I can say with certainty that this arduous task cannot be undertaken by the old, senile, and infirm. It must be shouldered by those with sound minds. However, a sound mind resides in a sound body, and to maintain a sound body, one must first practice hygiene.

This year is Children's Year, and we should pay even more attention to children's health. Children are the future masters of our country, and we need them to continue the work of saving the nation. Therefore, we should ensure that they first have strong bodies. According to a recent life statistics report from Nanjing, children under the age of five account for eight percent of the city's population, but deaths of children under the age of five account for 45 percent of the city's total deaths. In China, approximately 30 out of every 1,000 people die each year, meaning that about 12 million people die annually out of a population of 400 million. If we use the death rate of children under five in Nanjing as a proportion, then approximately 5.4 million children under five die each year nationwide. This clearly shows the importance of children's health.

To promote children's health, we should pay attention to the following points:

(1) Implement maternal and infant health—Whether a plant is good or bad depends on its seed; whether a person is virtuous or foolish, strong or weak, originates in childhood; and whether a child is healthy or not depends on their prenatal and postnatal care. Therefore, to promote children's health, we should simultaneously implement maternal and infant health measures, so that from conception to delivery, from infancy to adulthood, hygiene is always emphasized, and one is always nurtured by a hygienic environment. In this way, from birth to adulthood, their physical fitness will be very sound. Because health facilities are not yet widespread in our country, people in remote rural areas generally do not know what hygiene is. Each year, about 15 out of every 1,000 pregnant women die from puerperal fever because old-fashioned midwives are ignorant of human physiology and disinfection methods and deliver babies without knowledge. Additionally, about 200 to 250 out of every 1,000 infants under the age of one die from convulsions (neonatal tetanus) and other diseases caused by improper care before and after childbirth for similar reasons. In other countries around the world, the infant mortality rate in Japan is 132 per 1,000, in the UK it is 66 per 1,000, and in Australia, which has better health facilities, it is only 42 per 1,000. Our country's infant mortality rate is the same as that of England 250 years ago, but now England has reduced it to 10 percent. This further proves the importance of maternal and infant health.

(2) Improve the children's environment—As the saying goes, "One who stays near vermilion gets stained red, and one who stays near ink gets stained black." Children are particularly good at imitating, so it is essential to pay attention to whether the environment is suitable. In the past, Mencius's mother moved three times to educate her son, and Mencius became a rare sage throughout history. This is the benefit of improving the environment.

(3) Pay attention to children's nutrition—During childhood, the body has not yet fully developed, and extreme attention should be paid to nutrition. If nutrition is poor, the body will not only fail to develop fully, but will also suffer from certain deficiencies that can lead to weakness and disease. According to the results of physical examinations of students in primary and secondary schools in this city conducted by the Municipal Health Bureau, about 13 percent of the students have nutritional deficiencies. Even schoolchildren whose families are relatively wealthy have nutritional deficiencies, so the nutrition of out-of-school children and homeless children is even more unimaginable.

(4) Instill good hygiene habits in children—As the saying goes, "Habit becomes nature," and "Natures are similar, but habits separate people." This shows that good or bad habits are closely related to the development of a person's character. If children have good hygiene habits, their bodies will naturally become stronger.

(5) Popularize health education—Practicing hygiene does not necessarily require spending a lot of money; it may even be free. However, how to be hygienic? How to prevent disease? There must be adequate education to teach those who do not know this common knowledge, especially children, who should receive such health education.

(6) Vigorously implement children's health checkups—Whether a child's body is healthy or not is often unclear without a detailed examination, which reveals whether there are any deficiencies and where they are. Early diagnosis, treatment, and correction should be provided. The physical examination results of primary and secondary school students in this city show that many suffer from dental diseases and trachoma, followed by enlarged tonsils and then malnutrition. According to a survey by the National Health Administration of physical defects among primary and secondary school students in eight major cities across the country, about 52 percent suffer from trachoma, 41 percent have dental diseases, 25 percent have enlarged tonsils, 18 percent have swollen lymph nodes, 14 percent suffer from malnutrition, and 13 percent have vision problems. If such defects can be prevented in advance, their occurrence can be reduced. However, after they are discovered, regardless of their severity, if appropriate methods are used to treat them, they can be restored to health or saved from danger.

(7) Respect children's psychology—Although children are young and have limited experiences and incomplete thoughts, they often have their own unique psychology. They are innocent and genuine. Parents, elder siblings, and teachers should show empathy everywhere, treat them with sincerity, and provide appropriate encouragement and inspiration at all times. For example, when children express their personal thoughts or create something, they will feel interested. If, at this time, parents, elder siblings, or teachers adopt an adult attitude and dismiss it as childish, or ignore it, or talk about other things, or nitpick, or even punish them, this is a barbaric and rude act of trampling on children's pure souls, which will inevitably cause children to doubt or develop antipathy and prevent their thoughts from developing upward. The future happiness of children will inevitably suffer major setbacks.

(8) Promote school health—In the past, education mostly emphasized "teaching" and rarely paid attention to "nurturing." Now, education is gradually changing its focus to "nurturing." Promoting hygiene means emphasizing both "teaching" and "nurturing." All aspects of children's environment, habits, nutrition, health education, physical examinations, and correction of defects can be addressed in schools during their education. As for the health of kindergarten children, it should also be included in the list of things to pay attention to.

In short, children are the new hope of the nation and the future masters of the country. Special attention should be paid to the health of children, who are the new hope of the nation. This is my hope for this year's Health Campaign Congress! June, Year 25, Shanghai.

Preparation Process for the 15th Health Campaign 138

— Shen Gao

The preparation for this year's health campaign began in early May. Thanks to the support of all parties and the cooperative efforts of various organizations and groups, everything is now in order, and the opening ceremony is officially scheduled for today. I will now report on the preparation process and the special purpose of this year's campaign in summary, which may be of interest to all sectors.

This year's health campaign continues the experience of the previous session and adapts to the needs of the times. The organizational aspect is slightly different from the previous session in that the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association has joined and is working alongside the Health Bureau to fulfill similar efforts. In early May of this year, the Association received a notice from the New Life Movement Promotion General Association to hold a summer health campaign. Subsequently, Director Wu, the Association's instructor and mayor, stated that the city holds a health campaign every year, and although this year's campaign was approaching, he ordered it to be merged and held together, still named the 15th Health Campaign. After the Preparatory Committee's election, the Health Bureau and the New Life Movement Association were appointed as the chairman and secretary-general of the campaign, respectively, to oversee the preparations for this year's health campaign. Many organizations and groups participated in this Preparatory Committee, and they were assigned duties in accordance with the charter. A special list is shown below:

Health Campaign and National Revival 139

— Chen Diaoyuan

The health campaign is one of the seven campaigns promoted by the central government in recent years. Following this, Chairman Chiang promoted the New Life Movement, emphasizing cleanliness first and foremost, and the movement has swept across the country. Now, during the summer season, Shanghai is holding the 15th Health Campaign to promote the health of all citizens and seek the happiness of mankind. This is truly cause for celebration.

China's health undertakings have been prospering in modern times, providing a safeguard for human life. This barrier that protects our lives is constantly being advanced, and as a result, human happiness is also increasing with the progress of the health campaign.

Shanghai's health facilities are making increasingly significant progress. In terms of drinking water, there is good tap water, and the public is spared from the transmission of parasitic eggs and bacteria. In terms of nutrition, the commercially available food and beverages are subject to inspection and regulation by the competent authorities, so that people do not have to worry about buying rotten fish or meat. In terms of medical administration, doctors, pharmacists, midwives, and nurses must pass examinations and certifications. Hospitals, clinics, pharmacies, and drug dealers are also subject to the supervision of the competent authorities. The insurance system is also gradually expanding. All of this is based on the premise of the people's happiness. This shows that Shanghai is meticulous in its public health efforts for the public.

Public health has made considerable progress. However, family health and personal health are also of utmost importance and should not be delayed. It must be understood that hygiene protects individual life and eliminates all dirt and disease-causing microorganisms. Individuals are members of society, and they cannot live apart from society. They are always connected to all individuals or groups and to the nation and its people. If each individual has a healthy body and a spirit of self-improvement, and extends this to others, it will become a common practice, which will not only strengthen our bodies but also serve as the foundation for strengthening the country.

Today, the national crisis is becoming increasingly urgent, and those who conspire against us are becoming increasingly rampant. For the sake of reviving our nation, we must mobilize the entire nation, transform the nation's health, instill hygienic habits in everyone, develop strong bodies, and sweep away the old, weak, and sickly atmosphere. This must begin with enthusiastically participating in the health campaign. Therefore, we know that the foundation of our strength lies in hygiene. Hygiene is the most practical and most fundamental element for reviving the nation. Let us all strive together.

World Games Track and Field Representative Zhang Lingjia Disqualified, Decision Made on Three Substitute Track and Field Representatives, Li Huitang's Eligibility Question Under Investigation, Zhou Changxing to Attend Track and Field Events in Germany at His Own Expense 140

The China National Sports Association's preparations for our country's participation in this World Games are gradually being finalized. The entire delegation's departure is imminent. However, important matters such as paying respects at the mausoleum in Beijing and listening to instructions, as well as the selection of athletes by the Track and Field and Swimming Selection Committee, must be reported to the Board of Directors for approval. Therefore, the Association's Honorary Secretary-General, Shen Gangliang, sent letters inviting Standing Directors Chu Minyi, Hao Gengsheng, and Wu Yunrui to hold the fifth Standing Directors Meeting in the Association's conference room at 3:00 PM yesterday, and invited directors in Shanghai, Ma John and Song Junfu, to attend and discuss together. The meeting lasted for five hours before adjourning. The minutes of the meeting are recorded below:

Minutes of the Fifth Standing Directors Meeting of the China National Sports Association:

Attendees: Hao Gengsheng, Shen Siliang, Chu Minyi, Wu Yunrui; Observers: Ma John, Song Junfu; Chairman: Chu Minyi; Recorder: Shi Zhaokang.

A. Report Matters

Recent economic situation; Track and field team selection process and training situation; Swimming and race walking selection process; National martial arts and weightlifting training situation;

B. Discussion Matters

How should the delegation go to Beijing to listen to instructions and the flag-receiving ceremony be handled? Resolution: Decide to take the 7:55 AM train to Beijing on the 23rd to pay respects at the mausoleum and listen to instructions, and return to Shanghai at 5:00 PM in the afternoon. All affairs in the north and south will be handled by Directors Chu and Hao. Request to review and approve the selected candidates for swimming, track and field, and race walking. Resolution: Swimming: Chen Zhenxing and Yang Xiuqiong were selected as representatives. Race walking: Cai Zhengyi and Zhou Yuyu (both sent by this association), Zhang Zaojiu and Zheng Chengshan (both funded by the China Race Walking Association) were selected as race walking representatives.

(A) Track and field: Chuan Jincheng, Jia Lianren, Chen Baoqiu, Wu Bixian, Wang Shilin, Huang Yingjie, Liu Changchun, Dai Shuguo, Cheng Jin, Wang Zhenglin, Lin Shaozhou, Leng Peigen, Guo Jie, and Li Sen were selected as representatives.

B. Regarding the amateur eligibility issue, Director Ma reported that Zhang Lingjia had indeed been working in the library of the Physical Education Department of Tsinghua University since graduating last year. However, the title on his employment letter was mistakenly filled in as a physical education teaching assistant, which is inconsistent with amateur rules. In order to maintain amateur rules, it is requested that the Board of Directors make a public decision. Resolution: Stop sending Zhang Lingjia as a track and field representative to the World Games decathlon event, and no substitute representative will be sent.

C. Decision: Zhang Jiakui, Situ Guang, and Hao Youde were determined to be substitute track and field representatives to fill vacancies in order of priority.

D. In the pole vault event, Fu Baolu insisted on participating in the preliminary selection on the 7th of this month despite being ill. After a doctor's diagnosis, he was instructed to stop participating. The Selection Committee suggested that a supplementary test be conducted on the 16th of this month. Father Zha Wang Hezhi's pole vaulting performance was quite good. In order to select true talent, he was specially allowed to participate in the supplementary test at the same time as Fu Baolu. If both of them perform well in the supplementary test, in addition to sending the first place, the second place will be made a substitute track and field representative.

E. Zhou Changxing's request to attend track and field events in Germany at his own expense. Resolution: Zhou Changxing's performance is still good, so he is allowed to participate at his own expense.

Regarding the amateur eligibility of Li Huitang, captain of the football team, Honorary Secretary-General Shen reported that he had read in a Shanghai newspaper on May 29 that Li Huitang, captain of the football team, was suspected of violating amateur sports rules, and requested a public decision on how to handle this.

Resolution: Send a letter to Li Huitang himself, asking him to state the facts to the Association, and send a letter to the relevant newspaper to explain the truth and submit it for discussion at the next Board of Directors meeting.

In order to avoid athletes participating in this World Games from violating amateur sports rules, anyone who wishes to participate in various competitions and performances in the future must obtain a special permit from this Association before being allowed to participate. Should this be publicly decided?

Resolution: A permit from this Association must be obtained before being allowed to participate.

(A) Appoint Zhang Boling (convener), Hao Gengsheng, and Jiang Xiangqing as members of the committee to revise amateur sports rules. Resolution: Passed and designated Honorary Secretary-General Shen Siliang as an ex officio member.

(B) Appoint Ma John (convener), Xu Minhui, Chu Minyi, Wu Bangwei, and Song Ruhai as members of the National Sports Highest Record Review Committee.

Resolution: Passed and designated Honorary Secretary-General Shen Siliang as an ex officio member.

Mayor Wu and the German Consul-General in Shanghai Hosted a Farewell Reception for Our World Games Athletes Yesterday Morning 141

National martial arts athletes perform national martial arts and screen films

China Sports Association and three other organizations host a farewell banquet

Mayor Wu Tiecheng of this city and the German Consulate-General in this city hosted a reception for our country's World Games athletes at the Grand Cathay Theatre at 10:30 AM yesterday. Mayor Wu, German Consul-General Bernait, Chu Minyi, and others gave speeches and screened Olympic films. At 12:00 PM noon, the China Sports Association, the Jingwu Athletic Association, and the China Wushu Association hosted a farewell banquet for all the World Games athletes at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA. The details are recorded below:

A Glimpse of the Grand Occasion

The reception hosted by the mayor and the German Consul-General for the World Games athletes was held at the Grand Cathay Theatre at 10:30 AM yesterday. More than a thousand people attended, including athletes from our country who participated in the World Games in track and field, national martial arts, and weightlifting, as well as guests from all walks of life. The Chinese and German Boy Scouts maintained order, and the flags of the Chinese and German parties and countries were suspended above the stage, creating a solemn and warm atmosphere. At the beginning of the ceremony, the Chinese Kuomintang party anthem and the German National Socialist Party anthem were played, and everyone stood in solemn respect.

Mayor's Speech

Mayor Wu Tiecheng first delivered a welcoming speech. The original text stated: "Distinguished guests, athletes, the grand occasion of China's participation in the World Games is an unprecedented event in our country's sports history. The athletes this time have all come through strict competitions, and it is not an exaggeration to say that they represent the essence of China's sports world. Given the excellent results of recent tests, it is right to have high hopes for the success of the athletes. This time, you represent the motherland and travel across the ocean. In addition to bidding you farewell, we sincerely hope that you will strive to compete and return with honors, so that China's sports can share the world's glory with its inherent culture and art. However, the expression of the spirit of sportsmanship is more important than winning medals. When you compete with athletes from various countries, if you can adhere to the spirit of sportsmanship, then China's glory will be even more valuable than winning medals. The strict competitions you have undergone recently can prove that continuous efforts will definitely yield excellent results. When you compete with athletes from various countries, you should work hard. No matter what the result, this experience will be beneficial to your future progress. It can be asserted that Germany has made amazing progress in politics, economy, society, and military preparations in recent years. This World Games will be held in Berlin, and it is fortunate that you will have the opportunity to visit and broaden your horizons. The friendship between China and Germany has always been harmonious, and their ideas for maintaining world peace are particularly consistent. We hope that this trip will allow you to convey the goodwill of the people of Shanghai to the people of that country and to other representatives participating in the World Games. We wish you a successful expedition."

Speech by the German Consul-General

Next, the German Consul-General Kribai delivered a speech, stating briefly: "On behalf of my country's government, I extend my sincere congratulations to your country's World Games delegation. For this Olympic Games, which will be held in Germany this summer, I and the German organizations in Shanghai extend our sincere welcome and wish you success and enjoyment of the honor of the Games, and then a safe return home."

Speech by Bernait

Subsequently, Bernait, chairman of the Western Track and Field Committee, delivered a speech, stating briefly that Chinese sports have been developing gradually, and its equipment has also been improving day by day. He hopes that this participation in the World Games will be based on the spirit of sportsmanship and strive hard. Finally, Chu Minyi gave a speech stating briefly that the nine Chinese national martial arts athletes who participated in the World Games have already been selected. National martial arts are our country's inherent national essence and will be promoted to various countries around the world along with the World Games.

National Martial Arts Performance

Chu also introduced the national martial arts athletes' performance, which included: Jin Shisheng's Shaomo boxing; Liu Yuhua's Dragon Walk Sword; Chuan Shuyun's Fourteen Styles; Zhang Erding's Six Harmony Double Sabers; Zhai Lianyuan's Four-Way Chaquan; Wen Jingming's Flower Spear; Zhang Wenguang's Five-Way Chaquan; Kou Yunxing's Spring and Autumn Saber; Jin Shisheng's Single Saber; Wen Jingming and Zhang Wenguang's Opposing Fists; Kou Yunxing and Zheng Huaixian's Single Saber Advancing Spear; Zhai Lianyuan and Zheng Huaixian's Double Sabers Advancing Spear; Wen Jingming and Zhang Wenguang's Unarmed Spear Disarming; and Zheng Huaixian also performed the dance with the stone dumbbells. For a time, applause thundered, winning unlimited praise from the audience.

Screening of Films

Finally, Olympic films were screened, showing the evolution of the Olympics from Olympia in Roman times, as well as the locations of each Olympic Games, until the construction projects of the venue for the 11th Games currently held in Berlin, the scenery of various parts of Germany, and abridged versions of various sports. The scale was grand, and the audience praised it unceasingly. The event did not end until around 12:00 PM.

Banquet by Three Organizations

All the athletes and a part of the guests dispersed from the Grand Cathay and then went to the YMCA to attend the banquet hosted by the China Sports Association, the Jingwu Athletic Association, and the China Wushu Association. A total of more than a hundred people attended, including Chu Minyi, Wu Tiecheng, German Consul-General Kribai, Shen Gangliang, Hao Gengsheng, Li Dachao, Hu Puan, Zhang Xingbai, Shao Rugan, and the athletes. Chu Minyi presided over the event and delivered a farewell speech, extending his regards to the athletes.

Speeches by Guests

Next, German Consul-General Kribai gave a speech, which was translated by Su Huixiang, stating briefly: "Today, I personally watched the national martial arts performance, and its brilliance was unprecedented. I had previously seen national martial arts performances in the Chinese military, but they were not as wonderful as today's. This trip to Germany to perform will surely be welcomed. I wish you all a smooth journey." Finally, Hao Gengsheng, sports supervisor of the Ministry of Education, and Tong Xingbai of the Municipal Party Headquarters gave speeches. The meeting did not end until around 2:00 PM.

Quick Sketch of Sending Off World Games Athletes 143

The soccer players participating in the World Games have already departed. The basketball and swimming athletes have not yet arrived in Shanghai, and the track cycling athletes have not been announced. Currently, only the track and field and national martial arts athletes are in Shanghai. The German Consul in Shanghai and Mayor Wu Tiecheng jointly hosted a send-off event yesterday morning at the Grand Theatre. Many people attended, and the atmosphere was solemn. I think the purpose was to watch the historical films of the Olympics.

I arrived at the Grand Theatre at ten o'clock, and the inside and outside of the entrance were crowded with people. Boy Scouts were stationed at each entrance. Those with tickets walked into the main hall or upstairs with a satisfied look, under the imposing gaze of the "sentries." Those without tickets lingered at the entrance. There were also a "large number" of beautiful female guests.

At the entrance to the theatre, Boy Scouts held hands to block the way. "Female guides" temporarily transferred from the Cathay Theatre received the guests' tickets, and the Boy Scouts let you through. The "female guide" then led you to your seat according to the seat number on your ticket. Therefore, the entrance was always crowded, but everyone was very polite, following the order of arrival in a well-mannered way.

Around ten-thirty, the theatre was almost full. There were no fewer female guests than male guests. There were also many foreigners, probably all expatriates under the jurisdiction of the German Consul, under the banner of the swastika, including two or three German female students. The only female track and field athlete, Miss Li Sen, wearing a dark gray printed silk cheongsam, looked very simple and elegant. She entered with Liu Changchun, Wang Shilin, and others, and sat directly in front of the stage. The radio continuously played pleasant music, with the Olympic opening march playing until the curtain rose. In the center of the stage curtain was the German swastika flag with red background and black characters, with our national party flag on both sides. Everyone in the audience was dreaming of the "Olympics."

At ten thirty-five, the party anthem was played on the radio. Everyone in the audience stood up with a "whoosh." The anthem was played beautifully, not as monotonous as we usually hear in ordinary orchestras. After the party anthem finished, everyone stood up again with a "whoosh" less than a minute after sitting down. Foreign men and women, as well as a group of female students, raised their right arms diagonally, standing very solemnly and silently, respectfully listening to the German national anthem.

Mayor Wu appeared in front of the dark curtain and gave a speech in Mandarin, followed by an English self-translation; both were read from the original manuscript. After a round of applause, there was another round of applause. Like a gentleman in a "cartoon" painting, the German Consul Kreipe, wearing a swallowtail coat, strode out and gave a speech in German, followed by an English self-translation. Next was Mr. White, a leader in the Shanghai expatriate sports community, who gave a speech in the most fluent English. He wanted to say all his words in one breath, with very fluent and clear articulation; he really had something. A sports figure cannot be separated from the attitude of a sports figure. At the end, he said: "In victory, be a bright victor; in defeat, be a bright loser." Finally, Dr. Chu Minyi came out, wearing a white tight-fitting top and white breeches. He first gave a speech in Shanghai-style Mandarin, then suddenly switched to French, which all looked very unique.

After the speeches, there was a national martial arts performance. Three women and five men, wearing matching white spun silk clothes and pants, came onto the stage from behind the curtain. They first lined up and marched on the stage, directed by a gentleman in the corner of the stage. These were our national martial arts athletes attending the World Games. Then they came out individually to perform, either boxing, swordplay, or weapons, or sparring. We already knew how our national martial arts athletes would be playing at the World Games. Foreigners welcomed sparring the most, especially weapons sparring, with enthusiastic applause filling the room. One person who performed with "plates" received the most applause, and he became even more energetic.

The movie started, and everyone wanted to see the historical films of the Olympics. The opening scenes were several "ruin" shots and the memorial tower of a warrior wearing a flower crown, which was probably the place where the Greek Olympics originated. Then, the locations of each meeting since 1896 were shown, with subtitles indicating the scene of the meeting. After 1912, a cross suddenly appeared, standing in the misty smoke, indicating that the Sixth World Games were sacrificed in the fires of the European War. One shot for each session, this was probably history.

After the history passed, it was the preparation situation of the 11th German session. First, scenes of scenery from various places in Germany and various great buildings in Berlin were projected. If you want to admire these landscapes and buildings, you have to go to Berlin. After that, there were spectacular scenes of the winter sports of the next World Games, and the original sites, foundations, and construction of various other stadiums; behind each scene, the future competition situation was faintly lined up. These shots were connected with fragments of previous World Games films, symbolizing the future lively situation. Each shot was very beautiful.

After watching the movie, the so-called "Olympic historical film" did not impress me much. But the German's working spirit and propaganda methods made me admire them to the extreme. (Huai)

Children's Education and National Salvation Movement (I) 155

Municipal Education Director Pan Gongzhan Speaks on Central Radio

(Central News Agency) Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, was invited by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee to broadcast a speech on the Central Radio Station from 7:30 PM to 8:00 PM on the 14th, with the topic "Children's Education and National Salvation Movement." The full text of the speech is recorded below:

Today, at the invitation of the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, I will give a lecture on children's issues to everyone. The predetermined issue is "Children's Education and National Salvation Movement."

At present, China cannot deny that it has reached a very serious period of national crisis, and it is the final moment of life and death. All over the country, except for a few who are willing to be traitors and willing to be slaves of a conquered country, no one is not doing their best to save the country from the crisis. Although the responsibilities are light and heavy, and the tasks are different, the direction of progress and the goals to be achieved are exactly the same. In other words, at this moment of life and death, every member of the country is working hard in their own position. This has become a consistent phenomenon throughout the country. Originally, there is more than one way to save the country. As long as everyone contributes their strength to the country and works hard for the country, it will be called saving the country.

The work that we in the education sector undertake is to cultivate healthy citizens for the future and establish an unshakable foundation for the country for thousands of years. In the current environment, since the national crisis is so serious, then the healthy citizens we need to cultivate are of course citizens who are sufficient to cope with the national crisis environment and have the power to resolve the national crisis. The causes of past national crises are not one, and we don't need to mention them. However, the future rise and fall of the national fortune is on our shoulders. How heavy should our responsibilities be? Since the responsibility of educators is so great, then what is the situation of education in general elementary schools? Posting a few slogans, shouting a few slogans, or having a national salvation training week and a national salvation unit design, can it be said that it is education worthy of the revival of the nation?

We should know that this kind of unsustainable facility is only enough to arouse children's temporary excitement. Once the five-minute heat is over, the efficiency is equal to zero. It is by no means a truly effective and practical method, and it cannot be said to be the national salvation education we need. Therefore, Mr. Hu Hanmin, Chairman of the Central Standing Committee, once said, "Pay more attention to the preparation of strength, and don't just vent anger." This is really the golden rule for us to implement education during the national crisis. The education implemented in general elementary schools has committed the fault of "just venting anger." Originally, the work of saving the country cannot be effective in one day or one night. We must have continuous perseverance to do it before we can achieve results. If we use empty words to save the country and act emotionally, where can we get real and permanent effects? Education with the power to save the country cannot be effective with empty words, nor can it be successful with temporary excitement. Then, how can we implement it to achieve satisfactory results? In a word, it is necessary to put in persistent, long-term, and practical effort on the foundation and fundamentally. The so-called "ten years of reproduction" (that is, education), "ten years of training" (that is, teaching) is a good example for us to implement education during this national crisis. We should then follow this spirit and move forward.

Some people think that education during the national crisis must be changed to a new pattern. In fact, it is not necessarily needed, because the purpose of education in our Republic of China is "to enrich the people's lives, support the survival of society, develop the national economy, and continue the life of the nation based on the Three Principles of the People, so as to achieve national independence, universal civil rights, development of people's livelihood, and promote world harmony. This educational purpose is inherently in line with the needs of today's national crisis environment.

Economic Supplement

The Development and Calculation of War Expenses 156

— Zhang Yifan

"One" The Most Brain-Taxing Point

The gunpowder scent of twenty years ago has permeated the entire globe since the September 18th Incident. The general staffs of imperialist powers are now working on economic preparations for wartime. In order to avoid repeating past mistakes, they are meticulously organizing economic institutions suitable for the demands of war, extensively replenishing combat resources, and burying themselves in studying how to obtain strategic raw materials, accumulate necessary reserves, and stimulate new production. The so-called wartime controlled economy, wartime industrial mobilization, and wartime financial preparations are now being deployed in part or in full in various countries. What taxes their brains the most, and what they are most enthusiastic about researching, is the calculation of future war expenses.

Originally, the first financial problem a country needs to solve before entering a war is how much war expenditure needs to be prepared. Especially the emergency expenditures at the very beginning of the war must be planned and prepared in advance. But how much is needed? This is an important question. Furthermore, after the war begins, the continuous expenditure of war funds, according to the general situation, always increases sharply. But what is the rate of increase? And what is the height when it reaches the highest point? These are also important questions. Although this depends on the scale of the future war and the state of its development, to adapt to changes as they occur and make appropriate decisions. But there must be a general idea in advance. This is the lesson the European War taught them!

In the past, the characteristics of the major war preparations of various countries' general staffs mostly embraced the policy of quick battles and quick resolution. They denied the possibility of a long-term war, believing that the war in the first few months should be extremely tense. If victory is quickly achieved, all economic difficulties will be completely resolved. This gave rise to various practical effects: the conscription of the entire skilled labor force, the unrestricted requisition of agriculture, and, most importantly, the hope of waging war with mobilized reserves. They thought that war itself could adjust the preparations. However, reality denied their calculations. In order to cope with the conditions of a prolonged war and raise continuous huge expenses, they had to issue banknotes indiscriminately, sowing all the evils of wartime and post-war inflation. Not wanting to repeat past miscalculations, the imperialist financial authorities have once again delved into an old account of past wars, trying to discover how to make financial preparations adaptable to the development of the war. The calculation of war expenses has become one of the most brain-taxing and most enthusiastically researched issues for them.

These kinds of problems have now been brought before us due to the compulsion of the environment. However, no matter what, we want to seek precise and striving predictions, which in fact is always impossible. Only within the realm of possibility, based on the past records of various countries' wars and our own wartime experiences, can we speculate on the scale of future wars and the future trends of prices, and then estimate a standard from a general perspective. With a general standard, there can be a basis for financial standards, so that it can carry out its mission.

[Two] Three Paths

The methods commonly used to estimate the monetary amount of war expenses generally follow the following three paths:

Estimate the direct war expenses required for each battle, and extrapolate the degree of increase based on the war years; then extrapolate how much the future war will increase compared to the last war?

Divide the same war into several stages, and then observe how much war expenses are required in each period, and determine the degree of increase in each period; in order to determine the expenses for emergency expenditures as scheduled at the beginning of the war, and the rate of increase of continued war expenses, and the degree to which they reach the highest point.

According to past experience, the actual situation of peacetime military expenditures, and the customs and living standards of our country's social life, estimate the average amount of war expenses required per soldier per day during wartime; and then extrapolate to the total amount of war expenses for the whole in a certain period, or the whole period.

At the same time, when estimating future war expenses, also pay attention to the following relationships:

The difference between wartime expenses and war expenses. Wartime expenses include normal expenses, which cannot be cancelled, but must be saved and reduced as much as possible. War expenses are purely for maintaining the war. In order to ensure victory in the war, everything is exhausted to satisfy it.

The difference in living habits and living expenses in various countries. It is a reasonable method to refer to the war experiences of other countries to estimate the needs of one's own country's war. Because the tactics and formations have their own characteristics and secrets, but their trends are generally consistent. However, the differences in the social living habits and living standards of various countries must be distinguished. For example, American soldiers' living habits are much more extravagant than ours; at the same time, the American society's living standards are much higher than ours. Therefore, there is a big difference in the cost of rations for soldiers.

The difference in prices in various periods. Prices in the same space do not differ much; but prices at different times change greatly. If we use the war expenses during the European War as a standard, we must pay attention to the price difference between the past and the present. Not only that, wartime prices are bound to be more expensive than peacetime. And even in the same wartime, the prices in each period can vary greatly. Therefore, we must pay special attention to the estimation of war expenses.

The main mission of wartime finance is to obtain the currency that represents war expenses. Only by using currency can we obtain the materials needed for war. If one's own country lacks war materials and must rely on foreign countries, then one must also estimate the changes in exchange rates and freight costs.

With the national mobilization, the economic world will be aroused to great changes. On the one hand, people are panicked, and the entire economic world is plunged into a state of chaos. On the other hand, the peacetime economic organization is transformed into a wartime economic organization in order to adapt to the necessity of the environment. Overcoming the state of chaos and assisting the adjustment of economic organizations all require a large amount of capital, and the amount may not be less than the war expenses required at that time. Although this cannot be included in the direct war expenses, it must be estimated in advance and prepared accordingly.

Finally, it is also necessary to understand the relationship that the more developed science is, the more war expenses increase. Because future wars are a collection of the elites of modern technology, competing with the enemy's forces. The last European war was a specimen of mutual resistance using machinery and factory productivity. Therefore, wartime industry produces and destroys to adapt to the limitless consumption of war; the result is that war expenses reach an unbelievable number. And this phenomenon will be expanded more and more in the future.

[Three] Calculation of the Development Degree of General Trends

To use the first method to extrapolate, we must first estimate the cost of each battle since modern times. Nitti once made a comparison table of the costs of major wars from the nineteenth century to the European War. From this, we can see the trend of the development of modern war expenses. (Those marked with ▲ are omissions from the original table)

(Note) The material is based on the quotation from Yin Wenjing's "Extraordinary Fiscal Theory." According to Bogart, "War Costs and Their Financing," the former was originally 3 billion US dollars, which was calculated by dividing by 19.3 US dollars per US dollar. The latter was originally 7 billion US dollars, and the calculation method is the same. See my "History of the Great Powers' Disarmament Diplomacy and Combat" quoted. Published by World Book Company, originally 7.5 billion Japanese yen, calculated by dividing by 12.72 francs per Japanese yen. Based on the statistics of E. R. Seligam, the original amount was 210.935 billion US dollars. Calculated in the same way as above. See "Essaysin Taxation"

Here, it has clearly pointed out the trend that the war expenses of each battle have gradually increased sharply, and especially the most dramatic in modern times. Unfortunately, the extended dates of each war expense have not been calculated, so we cannot calculate the degree of increase in each war expense. Moreover, there seems to be an inconsistency in the magnitude of war expenses such as North and South America, and the gradually expanding trend. Regarding this point, we need to use Dr. Bogart's war expense table, which indicates the dates of the war, and re-examine the amount of daily war expenses. In Bogart's original table, there are still two small-scale colonial wars, but there are no figures for the European War; here, the former is presented and the record of the European War is added separately. However, the estimates of war expenses for the European War vary greatly among individuals. In order to make our speculation more accurate, the main statistics are listed together here.

From this table, we can draw the following important conclusions:

First: In the middle of the 19th century, the rate of progress of military weapons at that time was not as great as it is today; and the trend of prices was also more stable than today. However, the war expenses of each war increased more than the last. The smallest difference was an increase of two times. The largest was eight times.

Second: If we compare the cost of the Franco-Prussian War era (late 19th century) with the First European War forty years later, the rate of increase is even more alarming. According to Dr. Bogart's calculations, it increased 15 times. According to Professor Seligman's calculations, it increased 9 times. According to the calculations of British statistician Kitting, it increased 8 times. According to Japanese Sugimura Yohtaro's statistics, although it is the smallest calculated among all, it is also five times as much. Seligman's statistics are based on the official reports submitted by the financial authorities of various countries after deducting the normal national expenses during the war, so they are generally recognized as the closest to the facts, then there is a difference of nine times in the forty years before and after.
