The Problem of Wheat Flour Self-Sufficiency in Extraordinary Times 157

— Li Yinbei

In China, the South eats rice and the North eats wheat. Rice and wheat are equally important for the people's food, and there has never been any distinction. But in terms of the current situation: Japan has strengthened its troops in North China, and the international situation is no longer the calm and favorable weather of the past! The future of the people's food will also have extraordinary changes. Therefore, the bread problem will soon become one of the serious problems in my country's extraordinary times!

In peacetime, my country's wheat production is about 400 million dan per year. (Note 1) However, due to various reasons such as farmers' retention and inconvenient transportation, according to flour millers: my country's wheat production is only enough for the national flour mills to use for six months. This causes the flour mills to often worry about shutdowns due to lack of raw materials.

In extraordinary times, wheat-producing farmland is occupied by trenches, highways, airports, fortresses, and other military activities. In any case, it is enough to reduce wheat production. And modern tactics, the extension of the front line, are often thousands of miles: new types of trenches cannot be built without sacrificing a large amount of valuable farmland. In our possible prediction, at least 15% of the arable land is occupied by it. Assuming that this prediction is reliable, then my country's wheat production will inevitably be greatly affected. Now try to calculate the area of wheat planting in each province in the 24th year, estimated and published by the Central Serum Experiment Institute, and the situation of arable land reduction should be as follows: (Unit: Municipal mu) (Note 2)

From the above table, it can be seen that the reduction of arable land will directly affect the decline of wheat production. And the main wheat-producing area in my country is the so-called four central regions north of the Yangtze River and south of the Yellow River. The national flour mills also take the wheat production in the four central regions as the source. Now from the perspective of regional distribution in extraordinary times: the so-called four central regions are just right for the extraordinary regions in extraordinary times! In the event of an extraordinary incident, the reduction in wheat production will inevitably be more than this number.

Secondly, in terms of flour milling. In the 20th year of the Republic of China, there were 85 flour mills in the country. In recent years, the flour industry has not increased or decreased. According to the records of the Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance: in the first half of the 23rd year, there were 89 flour mills in the country, distributed in the four regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, Shandong and Henan, Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, and Hebei, Shanxi, Chahar, and Suiyuan. The annual flour production is about 55 million bags. (Note 3) But when it comes to extraordinary events, can the buildings of the flour mills survive under the overturned nest? We have no certainty about this. Even if it is fortunate to continue working normally, the source of raw materials will inevitably become a major problem. It must be known that when military transport is busy, where will there be spare boats and vehicles to take care of your wheat transportation? Therefore, the flour mills that can be put into operation will inevitably feel the difficulty of "internal transport not following, external transport not entering"! The clever woman can't cook without rice, and she has to be forced to shut down.

Third: In this environment, the price of wheat in the producing areas is bound to plummet due to being blocked by military transport and unable to be transported out. Unlawful traitors, taking this opportunity, buy it from the middle; attempting to disrupt the food organization in extraordinary times. Causing a lack of raw materials in the market, factories forced to shut down; workers unemployed, in order to achieve the purpose of disrupting the security of the rear.

On the other hand, flour consumers will inevitably increase substantially due to the convenience of long-term storage and portability. We also assume that 15% is the increase rate of flour consumers; then it is not difficult to calculate the demand for flour in extraordinary times. According to the records of the Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance: in the 23rd year of the Republic of China, the flour production of national flour mills was 55,232,000 bags. (Note 4) Now calculate with an increase in the flour production rate of 15%, then the national flour production must be 63,516,800 bags. In fact, this number is not reliable; because in the 23rd year, foreign flour imported into China was 595,748 dan; domestic flour imported overseas was 64,572 dan; the excess of foreign flour was 531,176 dan. (Note 5) If this number is added again, in any case, there must be 64 million bags of flour production to be sufficient.

Can the above prediction really meet the needs of extraordinary events? This is too easy! It must be known that the wheat production of the people will not be transported to the market grain by grain and flour by flour for processors to mill. According to Mr. Xu Peikun of the Shanghai Social and Economic Investigation Institute, the wheat transported to the flour mills for milling in the country is limited to 15% of the total wheat production in the rural areas with convenient transportation in the four central regions of my country. (Note 6) The rest of the wheat is kept by the farmers for their own use. The wheat retained by farmers for their own use is listed below: (Unit: Thousands of dan)

One dan of ordinary wheat can produce two bags of flour. The wheat retained by farmers for their own use in the 23rd year amounted to 315,728,250 dan: a part of the wheat inside is seeds, and a part of the wheat is for winemaking. But at least 300 million dan of wheat are milled as raw materials for their own flour. Assuming that 300 million dan of wheat are milled, then 600 million bags of flour can be produced. Weighing the population of my country, this number seems to be in line. From the above speculation, the flour production in extraordinary times will definitely not be enough for the flour production.

In summary. The wheat flour problem in extraordinary times is definitely not a trivial problem. What means do we use to adjust wheat flour self-sufficiency? Based on what I have seen and heard, I offer the following suggestions:

1. Limit the amount of wheat retained by the people;

2. Implement a joint guarantee and storage system for wheat;

3. Adjust wheat flour transportation;

4. Use private mills to adjust the flour milling industry;

5. Set a legal price for wheat flour;

6. Implement a fixed quota distribution system for wheat flour.

(Note 1) According to the estimate of the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute of the Ministry of Industry, the national wheat production in the 20th year was 398,040,000 dan, 411,120,000 dan in the 21st year, 396,200,000 dan in the 22nd year, and 371,445,000 dan in the 23rd year.

(Note 2): See the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute, Agricultural Information Report, Volume 3, Issues 3 and 6.

(Note 3): See Social and Economic Monthly, Volume 2, Issue 3, Table 2 on page 22.

(Note 4): See the same item as above.

(Note 5): See Social and Economic Monthly, Volume 2, Issue 3, Table 9 on page 28.

(Note 6): See Social and Economic Monthly, Volume 1, Issue 2, page 15.

(Note 7): The current year is based on the 371,445,000 dan estimated by the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute of the Ministry of Industry.

Securities: Public Debt Shows a Moment of Unease 158

From June 8th to 13th last week, the market price of the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange was hit hard again by the southwest calling for troops. Public debt is in a time of suspicion and shock. Furious waves and overlapping layers can be seen everywhere. However, since the currency reform last year, the scope of market speculation has been greatly reduced, and the financial community has mostly felt satisfied and no longer absorbed. The number of transactions has decreased, and the range of ups and downs is also relatively small. However, the amount is too large, and retail investors are busy selling. Therefore, although the forward period has one month's interest, the market price is lower than the recent period. To prevent arbitragers from getting started, the trend last week was mostly getting worse and worse. On Wednesday, due to the southwest mobilization, spot goods were dumped, and after a sharp drop, the four types of new low prices, B, C, D, and E, were discovered. On Thursday, many parties publicized peace and encouraged absorption. Short positions of No. 47 and 48 were all covered, and the price rose by one or two yuan. The multi-party struggle can be said to be a commendable remaining courage. On Friday, the peace talk was not accurate, and No. 47 and 48 were sold again, and the price dropped by about one yuan. On Saturday, the news was dull and tended to brew. Retail investors covered their short positions, and major investors raised their bids, and the price rose by about one yuan again. Looking at the overall situation, it is still difficult to be optimistic. The changes in the current situation will never be so simple. The futures delivery in June is only a few days away. In this unfortunate environment, mutual infighting will be very impressive. The result of the week's market price was mostly a drop of a few corners to one yuan. Cotton Yarn: US Cotton Spot Goods Are Stable and Futures Return Small 163

Indian Cotton Sells More and Also Falls

Yesterday, US cotton opened, and many shorts were closed. Brokers, mainland gangs, Liverpool, and the Far East sold. There was rain in the east, and each month fell by one to ten pound sounds. Then, the buying households stopped selling, and the same industry bought in, and a part of it improved. The close was firm, and the spot goods did not move, and the futures fell from not moving to falling by four pound sounds. The spot price of English cotton fell by 5 points, and the futures fell by 34 points. Indian cotton initially rose due to good news about US cotton, and then became weak because Japanese merchants and the public bought in and encountered manipulators selling May futures. It is estimated that Pingguoer fell by 0.25 to 0.5 rupees, Aomra fell by half a rupee, and Bairoxi fell by 1 to 1.25 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left (13th telegram)

Investigation: Smuggled Goods Flood and Prices Fall 164

The Indication of Various Commodity Price Indices in Shanghai

According to the report of the National Tariff Commission, compared with the previous month, the wholesale, export and import commodity price index and the cost of living index in Shanghai in May of the 25th year have slightly fallen. The percentage of the fall is the largest at 2.9% for exports, followed by wholesale at 1.4%, and imports and living expenses are the most moderate, all below 0.5%. In recent months, smuggling in North China has become more and more rampant. The types of smuggled goods were initially limited to velvet, cotton cloth, flour, kerosene, gasoline, and various groceries. The sales of smuggled goods were initially limited to North China, but now they have also invaded the Central China area. The price drop this month is probably related to smuggled goods. It is hoped that the government's recent measures to check the import and sales of goods will be effective in preventing them, otherwise the general commodity prices may continue to fall. The comparison of this month's various indices with the indices of the previous month and the same month last year is listed below.

Spring and Autumn

Seen and Heard 165

— (Xu Tian)

On a Sunday afternoon, with nothing to do, I decided to become a "road inspector." Walking along Wusong Road, taking my time, I reached the vicinity of the Triangle Small Vegetable Market and saw a child selling sugared plums. He held a basket in his right hand, filled with green plums, and another basket in his left hand, filled with sugared plums. Nearby were three Western children, around six or seven years old, who were playfully reaching into the basket of sugared plums, grabbing one or two, teasing the child, or throwing them randomly on the ground. The plum-selling child was distracted, preventing one from stealing but unable to prevent another. He wanted to scold them but they couldn't understand, and he couldn't bring himself to cry. Fortunately, an "amah" nearby saw what was happening and stopped them.

Alas! Isn't this a miniature of "the strong bullying the weak?"

A Visit to Tangjiawan 166

— Chen Liang

Under the large brown oilcloth umbrella, someone shouted, "Yellow croaker, ten coppers for one tael!" It went on and on without end.

Endlessly, everyone shouted like this. Selling bamboo shoots, selling goby fish, selling celery, selling… every stall in the market hoped that customers would come their way. The pitiful old woman, blind in one eye, selling bean curd sheets, sat alone shrinking in a corner, calling "Sir," "Madam," and other respectful titles to every man and woman carrying a vegetable basket. However, people passed by without paying attention. Sometimes, she would even hear,

"Now that new broad beans are out, who would eat your old bean curd sheets?" Such heart-piercing words.

In the crowded sea of people, there were nannies of wealthy families, purchasing clerks from commercial firms, housewives from modest households, and the wives of workshop owners. Under the large oilcloth umbrellas, there were the haggling and bargaining of tongues, disputes over the market scale and eighteen taels, the quarrels over adding a little extra and grabbing a little extra, and the mutual accusations of freshness and staleness. This formed the bustling scene of Tangjiawan.

On the edges of the street, piles of socks, piles of remnant fabrics, piles of undershirts… the voices shouting "special deals" were loud and resonant, attracting workers in short jackets, young women, and some honest folks looking for a bargain. One copper coin for a pair of silk-like socks, three copper coins for a foot of indanthrene blue fabric, three silver dollars for three linen undershirts. Many people looked, but few bought. Large-scale "foreign cloth shops" also put up signs saying "Buy one get two free." Electric fans [whirred, whirred], and the foreign signs and drums at the windows of the buildings mingled with the noise of the market, creating a chaotic din.

A strange cry, and the sesame ball in the child's hand was knocked to the ground. The Annamese man's face was full of veins and tough muscles. "Little devil, you Chinese scum…" A blow to the back of the head. The yellow and oily sesame ball was crushed under the Dunlop tire of a truck. Oh, the investment, the investment, the peddler's blood and tears…

Things like this happen too often; they are not unusual.

In the "simple canteen," there were some honest diners sighing and discussing "rent, charges, the shrewdness of passengers…" These were all rickshaw pullers. Three copper coins for a bowl of something called "fresh soup," seven copper coins for a bowl of rice. The white porcelain bowls and plates were indeed clean in terms of equipment, but for the rickshaw pullers, this was "not of great importance." Their only requirement was cheap prices. However, there were too few canteens for common people. This point should be praised about Tangjiawan.

Jiangwan Road at Dusk 167

— Rong Yu

The time is not in the morning, not in the daytime, not in the night, but only in the very brief moment of dusk.

The climate is not in the snow-covered winter, not in the hot long summer, nor on windy and rainy days, but on a clear and beautiful day in early summer.

Jiangwan Road is not as bustling as Nanjing Road, nor as mysterious as Sichuan Road, and certainly not as affluent and frivolous as Avenue Joffre. On a flat asphalt road, besides the occasional public bus, there are very few other vehicles. As for pedestrians, besides a few country people carrying shoulder poles, there are no other idlers. As for scenery, besides a few tall Western-style houses, the surrounding area is full of green fields. It is extremely quiet, one might even say a road with a strong rural atmosphere.

However, there are quite a few universities and middle schools on that road. Every evening at dusk, they, both boys and girls, always stroll in twos and threes. Some whistle, humming the latest love songs, some chat quietly, commenting on the good and bad of others, some chew on fruit and peanuts, some ride bicycles, and so on... In addition, there are endless patterns. In short: "They, both boys and girls, are happy, active, free..., just like 'the darlings of heaven'."

Among these happy angels, regardless of boys or girls, those who wear dark glasses and blue gowns are always students known as "moralists." Those in neat Western suits, sprinkled with lots of perfume, are sociable students. Girls wear collared shirts on top and men's-style bloomers on the bottom; boys wear shorts and long socks, sleeves rolled up high, revealing strong muscles. These are the athletes that everyone notices. Those who wear baggy Western suits, keep their hair long, and deliberately put on a romantic attitude, these are sure to be future artists and musicians. There are also all sorts of atypical figures, but I cannot describe them one by one. In short, they are all pacing, talking, laughing, and chewing on this road.

The night gradually deepens, and in their golden halls, in their deep palaces, all the electric lights shine brightly. Then this large group of princes and princesses are swallowed into these large buildings; Jiangwan Road returns to the quiet of just now.

Early Summer on Xujiahui Road 168

— Yi Min

A long and wide Xujiahui Road, its lower half is like a disheveled country girl, while its upper half is like a slender urban lady.

Because I admire the urban lady, I moved house a month ago—from its lower half to its upper half—right to the most charming and beautiful section. The houses are brand new, the road is asphalt, and along both sides of the road, there are neat rows of trees. Now that summer has come, the green leaves grow bigger every day, fluttering in the early summer breeze, though perhaps they are not fluttering. Perhaps they are smiling faintly at the beginning of summer. Sometimes—morning, noon, evening—a few birds chirp on the branches, as if complaining on my behalf. The worries in my heart are all taken out by them like a young woman reeling silk, and they also send me some fresh, happy, and sweet things in return. Indeed, the green leaves have been sun-dried into many bright eyes, and those bright eyes reflect thousands of silver rays, making me feel particularly happy.

As evening approaches, the sun hides away. At this time, I always go out and stroll alone on the road, seeing unfamiliar men or women covered by the green shade above, coming and going, a little busy like ants. However, if they leave, I let them go; if they come, I let them come. It has nothing to do with me.

After a while, the taste of dusk suddenly becomes thinner and fainter. The black night invades the whole world, and naturally this corner, this small corner—the most charming and beautiful section of Xujiahui Road—becomes dark in the same way. The street lights far and near, little by little, emit a faint light!

On the road, on Xujiahui Road, the pedestrians slowly become scarce, surrounded by silence. At this time, the early summer breeze, carrying the scent of early summer, blows in gusts, sending me all the way home, and I gently close the door.

The Spring and Autumn Editorial Department of Shen Bao

Visiting the Lida Academy Chicken Farm 169

— Ya Fei

The bankruptcy of our country's rural villages, although due to natural disasters, man-made calamities, and the devastation of heavy oppression and exploitation, the lack of development of rural side businesses is also a major reason. Therefore, I feel that if we want to save the rural villages, in addition to improving various other constructions, promoting rural side businesses is indeed an urgent task.

Yesterday, I went to Jiangwan to visit the Lida Chicken Farm, which was founded by the Lida Academy. It has quite a long history, and the farm was once destroyed by shelling during the January 28th Incident. They have made considerable contributions to agricultural and pastoral undertakings. In addition to this chicken farm, there is also an Art-Appreciation Farm and a Rural Service Department in Nanxiang, and there are also bee farms in Songjiang and Jiaxing. The academy also produces many books and equipment related to agriculture and animal husbandry.

The chicken farm is located on Lida Road in Jiangwan and occupies a large area. In addition to more than ten tall chicken coops, the farm is also covered with various fruit trees, purple clover, vegetables, etc. The purple clover is for bees to collect nectar, and the vegetables are feed for the chickens. There are currently more than 300 breeder chickens, including the Italian breeds "Leghorn," "Rhode Island Red," the American breed "Barred Rock," the Turkish breed "Tiger Chicken," and mixed breeds. As for Chinese chickens, there is only the Xiaoshan chicken breed.

Leghorns are pure white, and these chickens are considered the best among chickens. The hens weigh about five or six pounds each and lay eggs very diligently, averaging about 300 eggs per year, and can lay for six years. The roosters weigh seven or eight pounds and can mate with more than ten hens at the same time and can be used for five or six years, so breeders should prefer the Leghorn breed. However, although Leghorns are good chickens, they are prone to disease, so it is best to raise "mixed" breeds—which are the offspring of Leghorn hens and Xiaoshan hens. However, the first generation of this breed seems to have some differences; it is not until the third generation that its color and eggs are the same as Leghorn, and its physique is as healthy as Xiaoshan chickens.

After visiting each adult chicken coop, we went to the chick-rearing room. That was a wooden building, taller than the adult chicken coops. It housed hundreds of chicks, raised in four groups: one week, two weeks, three weeks, and eight weeks old. Each group has a nanny heater and a nanny thermometer; the humidity is above 90 degrees. It is managed by people day and night, and there is a statistical table on the wall that can be recorded and checked at any time.

The water containers and feeding charts used here are all specially made, and they have equipment to prevent fouling and fighting among chickens. In terms of feed, the main daily feed is barley, wheat bran, and pearl rice flour, as well as cow bone meal, milk powder, fish meal, meat meal, oyster shell powder, silkworm pupae, etc.; however, green grass and vegetables are also essential daily feed.

Finally, we visited the incubation room. It was not a very large room, with three hot water incubators and one table-top incubator. The hot water incubators can incubate 250 eggs each time, and the table-top incubator can only incubate 50 eggs at a time. All are incubated using scientific methods, and the incubation time takes about three weeks.

It is said that the chicken farm used to have more than a thousand breeder chickens of more than ten breeds. Since it was destroyed by the war, the managers were not responsible, so it has not been able to recover until now. The manager has now been replaced, and it is planned to increase the number to 1,000 this year.

I visited for a full two hours, and was guided and explained to by Mr. Guo, so the impressions I gained were very profound.

Dousha (mung bean) Dumplings from Dongshan 170

— Zhu Shaofei

Three years ago, a Dongting Native Products Company opened on North Zhejiang Road. It is said that they used to fry and sell mung bean dumplings from their hometown. However, when I heard this news and went there with my grandmother to taste these mung bean dumplings with the flavor of our hometown, it was very unfortunate that the company had already closed down.

On the more bustling streets of my hometown, you could always see such a steamy mung bean dumpling stall selling fried dumplings. The stall owner was always an old woman or a young woman. On one side, there was a small yellow clay stove, and on the other side, there was a small stone mill. When there were no customers, they would sit by the stall and cut "paper money". When there were customers, they would scoop out half a spoonful at a time of mung beans that had been soaked in water to remove the skin and slowly grind them into a bowl of flour, and then fry them in that flat-bottomed pot.

Mung bean dumplings are regarded as a precious snack. When guests come, in addition to serving a cup of Biluochun tea, you would go to the street to fry a plate of mung bean dumplings to treat the guests. For example, if you are going on a long trip tomorrow, your relatives will also send you a "yellow basket" of dried mung bean dumplings for the journey. If you are idle at home and have nothing to do, you can come to the street alone, have a glass of white liquor, and then fry a plate of mung bean dumplings, sitting half on the stall and chatting idly with the stall owner. Fortunately, it doesn't cost much money; a small dumpling is two copper coins, and a dumpling with egg is only ten or so coins.

I really love eating mung bean dumplings, especially fried with egg. I remember when I was a child, I would secretly take eggs from the egg bucket at home and go to the street to fry dumplings to eat. When my mother discovered that there were fewer eggs, she knew for sure that I had taken them to fry dumplings, and I would be scolded and beaten. It has been many years since I have eaten mung bean dumplings. It was during the time when it was my family's turn to go back to our hometown to sweep the ancestral tombs, which was a full four years ago.

The Love Story of a Switched Phoenix 171

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: Fragrant Grass First Entrusts Human Hearts to Delicate Ripples; Small Pavilion's Bright Moonlight Night Warmly Welcomes Initial Dreams

Menglan did not expect to meet him here. For a moment, she was undecided, and had no choice but to lower her head and hide behind a willow tree. Zhang Litian said, "The flowers I gave you have no other meaning. Because you have collected all the novels I have written in various magazines, you are truly my confidante. I know very well that you are a young woman oppressed by old-fashioned etiquette. I sympathize with you. But that doesn't matter. Isn't this a republic? We can stand up and pursue our freedom." Menglan wanted to reply to him with a few words, but she could not escape the common behavior of girls, and blushed and lowered her head, unable to speak no matter what. But then she heard Zhang Litian sigh and say, "It is really difficult to find a confidant in life!" Menglan heard these words clearly expressing his disappointment. So she struggled to say one sentence: "Do you think I am not your confidante? I have read almost every article you have published." As she spoke, she looked outside but could not see Zhang Litian. When she turned out from behind the tree, she saw him holding the apricot flowers behind his back, walking leisurely to a pavilion on top of a mountain. That pavilion was clearly one on Yuhuatai, and she forgot all reason and chased after him. However, when she reached the pavilion, there was no one there. Looking around, the sky was vast, and the wind blew whistling on her, ruffling her clothes. Anxious, she tried to hold down her skirt. But the wind was blowing so hard, she couldn't hold it down no matter what. Anxious in her heart, she opened her eyes. Where were the willow trees? Where was Yuhuatai? It turned out it was a dream. Earlier, she had been greedy for the moonlight, and the windows had not been closed. The wind came straight to the bed, and so it ruffled her clothes. She sat up, rubbed her eyes, and saw only the moon, as big as a plate, hanging in the blue sky. In the sky, besides two or three big stars, accompanying the moon, there was not a single cloud. She went to the window and looked out. The roofs of other people's houses were all silent under the moonlight. The willow tree in her dream had a layer of green light and swayed gently in mid-air, as if saying, "Girl, I saw you dreaming." Looking up again, the sky seemed brighter. The moon was as small as a silver coin, and outside the building was a cold light, slightly tinged with smoke. It connected with the vague buildings in the distance. There were no lights inside the building, and the moonlight shone on the floorboards, painting a square of silver lacquer. The light reflected on the books on the bookshelf, the flowers in the vase, and even the bedding on the bed, adding a kind of secluded charm. She did not hear human voices, but only the rustling of the banana trees in the courtyard downstairs as they were swayed by the wind. Looking down at the courtyard, the shadows of the trees were dark, looking like a dreamscape. A person with a heart full of troubles, having just come out of a dream, cannot help but be stunned. (34)

Talk Less

A Few Words in Response to Mr. "Jin" and Mr. "Jia Zai" 175

— Respectfully,

The day before yesterday, I read a news article in the newspaper stating that students in Beiping were preparing for a demonstration. I couldn't help but feel saddened, so I wrote a piece titled "Thoughts on the Student Demonstration Movement in Beiping." After writing the title, I wanted to start writing the article, but difficult questions flooded my mind. If I supported this action, not only could I not, but I also wouldn't be able to. Please forgive the readers for the reasons why I cannot and should not, as I will not explicitly state them. If I opposed this action, it would naturally displease the general readership, who would think that at this point, opposing such actions would mean my blood was too cold.

However, the title had already been written, and the article had to be done. So, I decided on my intention, turned my pen, and wrote down the words from the day before. Let me restate the meaning of this article! My patriotic feelings, please forgive my presumptuousness, dare not lag behind others, to borrow the words of fashionable people. Compared to the patriotic students, they are even more serious. However, I ask myself, the country is impossible to love, and there is no way to love it, so I have diluted my patriotic feelings and instead gone to love the students. Furthermore, seeing or thinking about the forms of past patriotic movements, each one was more tragic than the last, and each one's effectiveness decreased each time. Moreover, what kind of Beiping and Tianjin are they now? Under the oppression of two forces, I fear there is no room to breathe. Is there even a place for you to demonstrate? So, unknowingly, I added the words "unnecessary" to the title and the words "respectfully inform" above the title. The words "thoughts" also had to be declared cancelled.

Unexpectedly, after this article was published, I received two letters from Mr. "Jin" and Mr. "Jia Zai," both criticizing me for holding improper views and absurd wording. The most absurd passage in my writing, I will now examine myself and confess my sins to Mr. "Jin" and Mr. "Jia Zai."

It is said, "The rise and fall of a nation is the responsibility of every individual." The heart of patriotism is shared by all. Precisely because the heart of patriotism is shared by all, students do not need to demonstrate alone. If we speak of responsibility, then the government's responsibility is, after all, a hundred or a thousand times heavier than that of students. Therefore, the government's patriotic heart should also be a hundred or a thousand times greater than that of ordinary people. Why should students seek trouble for themselves and do this meddlesome thing?

I knew this passage was absurd when I wrote it. After Mr. "Jin" and Mr. "Jia Zai" raised questions, I reread it and felt it was even more absurd.

Fortunately, this is just a small section of the newspaper. If what I said is right, no one will believe it or act upon it. If what I said is wrong, everyone will just laugh it off. Please don't take it too seriously. As for the words "cynical remarks" in my article, they come from here. The so-called cynical remarks are irresponsible remarks and worthless remarks. That is all I meant.

However, if viewed or interpreted from another perspective, the location of responsibility is even clearer. I don't need to add anything unnecessary or repeat myself now.

Small Scenes of Life 176

— Shi Feng

I'm starting to feel scared: A whole year, since I left home. Looking back at this not-so-short road, it really makes my timid heart tremble.

Every day, when I'm like a smoked-out cigarette, thrown onto the bed by exhaustion, the remaining fire in my heart still burns. I want to read a book, take the magazine that a well-meaning friend sent

Page 20

with a "please criticize" note, and hope to get some comfort. But, when I see the third line, my eyes involuntarily close, and the hand holding the book is as soft and powerless as cotton. The book falls heavily beside the pillow. Alright, I'll just relax for now, resting a bit is not too late. A person who works all day really needs to rest, and I work with both my mind and body, so I really should rest well. But, I can't just go to sleep, I want to close my eyes for a bit and read later.

The sound of a car horn wakes me up.

I'm still lying in bed, the book under my head. I have no strength in my body at all, I wonder if death is just a little more powerless than this.

The car has passed: carrying the lonely wind of the night towards the distance.

The alley is quiet, without a sound; is everything dead? No, the policeman's leather shoes are ringing: Kang, Kang,... But, what's contained in this sound isn't anything beautiful, but disturbing the quiet that others desperately need. Such a monotonous and irritating sound!

I lie in bed, looking at the light, it's lonely and timidly shining. Outside is the dark air, and cold air occasionally blows in, the light flickering uncertainly. I think of the mourning hall after a person dies: that gloomy and mysterious room... I also think of that friend who works as a gatekeeper, he's already forty years old, half of these forty years he spent traveling, and crossed a mountain from the Songhua River to a new country; he works as a gatekeeper in a small port full of exotic customs near the Songhua River. At that time, he was poor of course, and every night in the deep hours, he always strummed his year-round companion: that lovely "guitar"! Singing newly learned verses with a sentimental and passionate tone. He's a poet, a poet entranced by the wandering life...

The gatekeeper in our alley is a Shandong person. Really, whether in speaking or doing things, I haven't had any good feelings.

Just listen to his monotonous and irritating sound: Kang, Kang,...

I want to prop myself up to close the window, firstly to block the wind, and mainly to isolate this sound.

I hope no one will disturb me, and let me properly recall this past year of life. But I don't want to move at all. My eyes are wandering around the things on the table, on the chair, and the photos and calendar hanging on the walls, they all seem to be intimately keeping me company, and, they seem to be asking me good night, as if they haven't seen me in a long time. I want to raise my hand to caress them, but I don't have the strength. So I unconsciously close my eyes again. (To be continued)

Facts about Face Powder 178

— Written by Sanhua Company

Q: How to test the quality of face powder?

A: Two tests must be performed. The first is to test the quality of its ingredients to ensure they are refined and harmless. This can only be done in a well-equipped chemical laboratory. The second is to test by oneself. That is, women should test it on their facial skin. Therefore, when choosing face powder, one should pay attention to two major factors: the purity of the quality and its performance on the skin.

Q: How to judge the quality of face powder?

A: All face powder must contain extremely pure ingredients and must be manufactured under skillful management. It must also adhere firmly to the skin, so that it can avoid the invasion of wind, sun, and dust, and be suitable for dry, oily, and generally normal skin. Furthermore, it must be able to remove shine and create a "snowy" beauty on the face.

Q: Why must powder be applied especially to the nose and cheeks?

A: Because these two parts are most prone to sweating. This situation can only be corrected by using a face powder that contains ingredients that absorb sweat and adheres firmly. The face powder refined by the American Sanhua Company contains this special ingredient, so it is most suitable.

Q: Can face powder clog pores?

A: This depends on the type of face powder used. Inferior face powder swells when its powder comes into contact with the skin's natural moisture, so it is especially easy to clog delicate pores when applying this type of inferior face powder in the summer. However, there is absolutely no need to worry about such inferior ingredients when using Sanhua Company's face powder.

Q: Why does face powder often clump on the face?

A: Inferior face powder often has this phenomenon. There are three reasons. First, the powder lacks water-absorbing properties, and sweat turns the face powder into a thin layer of paste. Second, the powder contains starch, which swells when it gets wet with sweat, causing the skin to appear mottled. The third reason is even more common, that is, most face powders cannot adhere firmly to the skin, making them easy to clump. Therefore, it is necessary to reapply powder from time to time, and the layers of powder naturally accumulate unevenly, which is especially true in summer. Usually, using a suitable cream as a powder base can achieve a smooth and even effect.

Q: My daughter is sixteen years old and has beautiful skin. I don't know if using face powder will damage her appearance?

A: This also depends on the type of face powder used. High-quality face powder not only does not harm the skin but can also protect it. This protection is especially needed for young women who want to maintain their youthful beauty.

Q: What is the effect of face powder on dry and oily skin?

A: If the face powder has the quality of adhering firmly, it can protect it. This is because dry skin is most suitable to avoid the invasion of wind, sun, and dust. In other words, it avoids the causes of dryness. As for oily skin, in addition to being protected by a firmly adhering face powder, a special powder quality is also needed to prevent oiliness from causing shine on the skin. The above two characteristics are both effective parts of Sanhua Company's refined face powder.

Q: Before actually trying it on one's own face, is there any way to determine which powder color is most harmonious with one's skin tone?

A: When buying face powder, if you need to determine a certain color and do not want to remove the original makeup, you can apply the powder puff to the upper part of the wrist on the arm to determine it. This test is most likely to allow people to choose the most suitable powder color. However, if the color of the clothing changes, then the powder color used will sometimes also need to be harmonized with the clothing color for coordination.

Q: When should both dark and light powder colors be used together?

A: For example, applying dark-colored face powder to the contours of the face can make it look smaller. If the nose is too large, applying a powder that is darker than other parts of the face can make the nose look smaller. If the face is too narrow, applying light-colored powder to the part where the eyes and nose intersect can correct it. As for those with broad faces, they can apply dark-colored powder along the hairline, which can reduce the degree of broadness.

Q: What is the best way to draw eyebrows?

A: When drawing eyebrows, first remove any powder marks around the eyebrows, then use an eyebrow pencil to draw a thin line, which should be slightly upward and outward, drawing a long stroke. If the natural eyebrows are too short, they should be slightly extended, but the eyebrows should be extended slightly upward, so that the space between the eyes can appear wider.

Q: How can lipstick be used to its fullest potential?

A: A fully exposed oral cavity is the most beautiful. Therefore, the so-called "Cupid's bow" should be fully apparent. Those with thin lips can apply more lipstick to the upper lip to correct it. Those with thick lower lips should move the powder line up a little. When applying lipstick, you should first apply it to the middle and move outward, gradually becoming lighter. If you use Sanhua Company's lipstick, the lips can be more moist, soft, and bright. This is the trend of today's fashion.

Central-Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Romance of the Three Kingdoms, Changban Slope"

Eternal hero, Zhao Zilong. He charged into battle alone, with his spear. He was willing to risk his life to save the young lord, charging into Cao's camp. The snow-white robe was stained red with blood. Seeing him, his tiger eyes flashed with anger, and his spear pierced wildly. Seeing him, his precious sword waved, his spirit soaring like a rainbow. Riding into the encirclement. The loyal servant was full of courage. Scared, Cao Cao's heart and soul were broken. He inquired as to his name, and sent Cao Hong. He cherished talent and could not bear to harm him. He ordered the entire army to capture him alive as a great achievement. Who knew that while Cao Cao's wish might be fulfilled, cold arrows would be launched from the side. He was all courage. The enemy soldiers were thousands upon thousands surrounding him. He found the ruined well. Seeing the mistress before him, he bowed. Several times he knelt to help her onto the horse. But Lady Mi jumped into the well. Zilong quickly hid Adou, then tied him up securely and placed him close to his chest. Suddenly, two enemy generals rushed over. Zilong drew his spear, mounted his horse, and fought bravely. In an instant, he speared and slashed the brave generals to death. He could only go to Changban Slope to find his lord. A rider sped along, dust blinding his eyes. He heard the drums beating loudly. Suddenly, he saw Zhang Fei standing with his spear. Blocking the general and not letting him pass. Asking him where he was stationed.

Movie News

"Ten Thousand Wonders Troupe" and "Removing Evil for the People" 183

Two Great Contributions from the Shanghai Grand Theater

The Shanghai Grand Theater on North Sichuan Road, in order to cater to the interests of all circles, spared no expense in hiring the Ye Ming Dance Troupe "Ten Thousand Wonders Troupe." From today, all the male and female actors will perform various new programs day and night. The most exciting of these is "King Kong Resurrection," which is the crystallization of the troupe's efforts. It is the first time it will be performed in Shanghai. It is novel, interesting, and deeply meaningful. It cannot be compared to the mediocre songs and dances of today. It is truly creating a new voice in the world of song and dance. Furthermore, it is specially showing the latest Columbia martial arts blockbuster "Removing Evil for the People," starring martial arts star Buck Jones and beautiful actress Helen Mack. It is the first public screening in Shanghai. It is a masterpiece that makes the two outdated films stand out. It is brave, enthusiastic, and filled with superhuman intelligence. The entire film is in an extremely tense state. Famous films and songs and dances are contributed at the same time. It is said to be a new record for the first-run theaters, so the shows have been very crowded for several days.
